This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Brothers_Osborne","to":"Brothers Osborne"}],"pages":{"40828792":{"pageid":40828792,"ns":0,"title":"Brothers Osborne","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music group}}\n{{for|the Kentucky bluegrass group of the 1960s and 1970s|Osborne Brothers}}\n{{good article}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=March 2024}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Brothers Osborne\n| image           = Brothers Osborne (cropped).jpg\n| alt             = Country music duo Brothers Osborne at a concert in 2018.\n| caption         = John Osborne (left) and TJ Osborne (right) at [[DTE Energy Music Theatre]], June 2018\n| origin          = [[Deale, Maryland]], U.S.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/5687069/bubbling-under-the-colourist-breaks-through-at-alternative|title=Bubbling Under: The Colourist Breaks Through At Alternative|date=September 6, 2013|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=October 18, 2013}}</ref>\n| genre           = {{Flatlist|\n* [[Country rock]]<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.vulture.com/amp/2021/02/tj-osborne-brothers-osborne-gay.html |title=TJ Osborne of Country Duo Brothers Osborne Comes Out As Gay |last=Curto |first=Justin |date= February 3, 2021 |publisher= Vulture |access-date=September 26, 2021 }}</ref>\n* [[Country music|country]]<ref name=\"allmusic\"/>\n}}\n| discography = [[Brothers Osborne discography]]\n| years_active    = 2012\u2013present\n| label           = [[Capitol Records Nashville|EMI Nashville]]\n| current_members = John Osborne<br/> TJ Osborne\n}}\n'''Brothers Osborne''' is an American [[country music]] duo consisting of brothers TJ Osborne (lead vocals, rhythm guitar) and John Osborne (lead guitar, background vocals). Born in [[Deale, Maryland]], the duo signed a recording contract with [[Capitol Records Nashville|EMI Records Nashville]] in 2012 and began releasing music the following year. Their 2015 song \"[[Stay a Little Longer (Brothers Osborne song)|Stay a Little Longer]]\" became a top five hit on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] and [[Country Airplay]] charts, and their success led to the release of their debut studio album titled ''[[Pawn Shop (album)|Pawn Shop]]'' the same year. Since then, Brothers Osborne have released the albums ''[[Port Saint Joe (album)|Port Saint Joe]]'' (2018), ''[[Skeletons (Brothers Osborne album)|Skeletons]]'' (2020), and ''[[Brothers Osborne (album)|Brothers Osborne]]'' (2023).\n\nThe duo have since had further hits with \"[[It Ain't My Fault (Brothers Osborne song)|It Ain't My Fault]]\" (2017), \"[[Shoot Me Straight]]\" (2018), and \"[[All Night (Brothers Osborne song)|All Night]]\" (2019), and as featured artists on [[Dierks Bentley]]'s \"[[Burning Man (song)|Burning Man]]\" (2019). Along with their own songwriting, their musical success is credited to producer [[Jay Joyce]]. Artists with whom they have worked include [[David Nail]], [[Lee Ann Womack]], and [[Lucie Silvas]] (the latter of whom is John's wife). Their musical style takes influence from [[Southern rock]] and [[outlaw country]], with particular emphasis on the styles of TJ's lead vocals and John's guitar playing. The duo attracted further media attention in February 2021 when TJ [[coming out|came out]] as gay, making him the first openly gay artist on a major country music label.\n\n==History and formation==\nBrothers John Osborne (born 1982) and TJ Osborne (born 1984) were two of five children raised in [[Deale, Maryland]], a rural fishing community located along the [[Chesapeake Bay]].<ref name=\"whitburn\">{{cite book|last=Whitburn|first=Joel|title=Hot Country Songs 1944 to 2017|publisher=Record Research, Inc|year=2017|page=56|isbn=978-0-89820-229-8}}</ref><ref name=\"The Boot\">{{cite web |last1=Allers |first1=Hannahlee |title=Brothers Osborne Talk Childhood in Maryland |url=https://theboot.com/brothers-osborne-maryland/ |website=The Boot |date=September 21, 2014 |access-date=March 3, 2021}}</ref> In addition to their parents, who both wrote and played music regularly, their uncles and cousins also pursued musical hobbies. The family often gathered to perform music, inspiring the brothers' earliest musical aspirations. \"Naturally, John and I wanted to participate and play with the family because it was fun. And that was where we cut our teeth,\" said TJ Osborne in 2014.<ref name=\"CMT\">{{cite web |last1=Parton |first1=Chris |title=Brothers Osborne's \"Rum\" Toasts Maryland Rednecks |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1730845/brothers-osbornes-rum-toasts-maryland-rednecks/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150107133417/http://www.cmt.com/news/1730845/brothers-osbornes-rum-toasts-maryland-rednecks/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=January 7, 2015 |website=[[Country Music Television]] |access-date=March 3, 2021}}</ref> The brothers then started performing regularly with their father, John Osborne Sr. Together, they played in a band called ''Deuces and a Quarter,'' while also helping their father with his day job as a [[plumber]].<ref name=\"Baltimore Sun\">{{cite web |last1=Case |first1=Wesley |title=With higher profile, Maryland natives Brothers Osborne return to Grammys |url=https://www.baltimoresun.com/food-drink/bs-ae-brothers-osborne-grammys-20170209-story.html |website=[[Baltimore Sun]] |date=February 10, 2017 |access-date=March 3, 2021}}</ref> When not performing, the brothers practiced music in their family's backyard shed.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/brothers-osborne-mn0003176030/biography|title=Brothers Osborne|last=Collar|first=Matt|work=[[Allmusic]]|access-date=July 11, 2015}}</ref>\n\nThe duo continued performing more consistently through high school. They later represented their high school in the [[Anne Arundel County]] \"Battle of the Bands\" in 2000.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.capitalgazette.com/lifestyle/ph-ac-cn-totw-watn-john-osborne-1231-20161225-story.html|title=Teens of the Week: John Osborne now a rising country-Western music star|last=Winters|first=Wendi|website=capitalgazette.com|language=en-US|access-date=June 17, 2019}}</ref> Upon graduation, John attended [[Belmont University]] in [[Nashville, Tennessee]]. TJ soon followed his brother to the city after finishing high school.<ref name=\"Baltimore Sun\"/> They first attempted to have separate careers. John began playing gigs as a sideman, while TJ played [[Double bass|upright bass]] and composed material for other artists. TJ also made several [[Demo (music)|demonstration records]]. Yet his own voice was considered \"not generic enough\" for many industry professionals. It was after this that the brothers started working together.<ref name=\"Metal Hammer\">{{cite web |last1=Glass |first1=Polly |title=From prog metal to folk and the Foo Fighters: how Brothers Osborne paid their dues |url=https://www.loudersound.com/features/from-prog-metal-to-folk-and-the-foo-fighters-how-brothers-osborne-paid-their-dues |website=[[Metal Hammer|Louder Sound]] |date=December 2020 |access-date=March 3, 2021}}</ref> For several years, the duo performed in clubs, bars, and other small music venues.<ref name=\"Baltimore Sun\"/> In 2011, they signed a publishing contract with [[Warner Chappell Music|Warner-Chappell]].<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> In 2012, the siblings secured a recording contract with [[Universal Music Group Nashville|EMI Nashville]], a subdivision of [[Capitol Records]] and Nashville's [[Universal Music Group]].<ref name=\"Washington Post\">{{cite news |last1=Yahr |first1=Emily |title=Meet the Brothers Osborne, the embodiment of country music's evolution |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/lifestyle/style/meet-the-brothers-osborne-the-embodiment-of-country-musics-evolution/2016/01/20/b8d0ffda-b950-11e5-99f3-184bc379b12d_story.html |newspaper=[[Washington Post]] |access-date=March 3, 2021}}</ref>\n\n==Career==\n===2013\u20132016: Career rise and ''Pawn Shop''===\nIn 2013, Brothers Osborne released their debut single titled \"[[Let's Go There]].\" The uptempo song became a minor hit, reaching the top 40 hit on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] chart. Its limited radio success enforced their record label's decision to not release an album.<ref name=\"Washington Post\"/> The song was followed in 2014 by the single \"[[Rum (song)|Rum]].\"<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> It reached a similar ''Billboard'' chart position, which continued to halt an official album release from EMI. Instead, the label released a [[Brothers Osborne (EP)|self-titled extended play]] later that year.<ref name=\"Washington Post\"/> The EP reached the top 25 of the ''Billboard'' [[Top Country Albums]] list and contained five tracks (including their 2014 single).<ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Brothers Osborne'' chart history (Country Albums) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/clp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 4, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=''Brothers Osborne'': Brothers Osborne: Songs, reviews, credits |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/brothers-osborne-mw0002749126 |website=[[Allmusic]] |access-date=March 4, 2021}}</ref> Following its release, several music journalists named the pair on new artists lists, such as \"Best of What's Next\" or \"Ones to Watch.\"<ref name=\"Washington Post\"/> Hannah Smith of ''Vinyl'' magazine praised the project and anticipated future success for the pair: \"Brothers Osborne is a duo who are redefining the lines and following in the footsteps of trailblazers who have launched a revolution with their distinct music.\"<ref>{{cite web |last1=Smith |first1=Hannah |title=Brothers Osborne: ''Brothers Osborne EP'' |url=http://vinylmag.org/2014/09/16/brothers-osborne-brothers-osborne-ep/ |website=Vinyl |date=September 16, 2014 |access-date=March 4, 2021}}</ref>\n\nTheir third single \"[[Stay a Little Longer (Brothers Osborne song)|Stay a Little Longer]]\" was issued in 2015. The song was originally included on their 2014 EP, but was re-recorded for the single release.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/><ref name=\"stone\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/brothers-osborne-on-country-music-people-are-tired-of-the-bullsh-t-20150330#ixzz3fGAYNlJ0|title=Brothers Osborne on Country Music: 'People Are Tired of the Bullsh-t'|last=Hudak|first=Joseph|date=March 30, 2015|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=July 8, 2015}}</ref> \"Stay a Little Longer\" became the duo's first major hit, reaching the top five of the ''Billboard'' country chart.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> Its success led to the release of their first full-length album titled ''[[Pawn Shop (album)|Pawn Shop]]'' (2016).<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> The album contained material mostly penned by John and TJ Osborne. It also featured vocal collaborations with [[Lee Ann Womack]].<ref name=\"liner\">{{Cite AV media notes |title=Pawn Shop |others=Brothers Osborne |year=2016 |type=CD booklet |publisher=EMI Nashville |id=B0022364-02}}</ref> ''Pawn Shop'' peaked at number three on the ''Billboard'' country albums chart and number 17 on the Billboard 200.<ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Pawn Shop'' chart history (Country Albums) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/clp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 5, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Pawn Shop'' chart history (Billboard 200) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/tlp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 5, 2021}}</ref> ''Pawn Shop'' received four stars from [[Allmusic]]'s [[Stephen Thomas Erlewine]] who called it \"busy, but never overstuffed.\"<ref>{{cite web |last1=Erlewine |first1=Stephen Thomas |title=''Pawn Shop'': Brothers Osborne: Songs, reviews, credits |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/pawn-shop-mw0002902920 |website=[[Allmusic]] |access-date=March 5, 2021}}</ref> Andrew Unterberger of ''[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]'' commented that the album was \"setting the bar for the genre in 2016.\"<ref>{{cite web |last1=Unterberger |first1=Andrew |title=Review: Brothers Osborne Take Country to the 'Pawn Shop,' Leave With Something New |url=https://www.spin.com/2016/01/review-brothers-osborne-pawn-shop/ |website=[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]] |date=January 11, 2016 |access-date=March 5, 2021}}</ref> Two additional singles were spawned following the record's release that later became hits: \"[[21 Summer]]\" and \"[[It Ain't My Fault (Brothers Osborne song)|It Ain't My Fault]].\"<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> The commercial success led the brothers to win five industry awards. Both the [[Academy of Country Music]] and [[Country Music Association]] named them as Vocal Duo of the Year in both 2016 and 2017, with the latter association also awarding New Vocal Duo in 2016.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> Also in 2016, the brothers co-wrote and sang on the track \"Good at Tonight\" on [[David Nail]]'s album ''[[Fighter (David Nail album)|Fighter]]''.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Skates|first1=Sarah|title=David Nail Reveals Track List For New Album, 'Fighter'|url=http://www.musicrow.com/2016/06/david-nail-reveals-track-list-for-new-album-fighter/|access-date=June 2, 2016|work=[[MusicRow]]|date=June 1, 2016}}</ref> This song was also released as a single, charting at number 52 on Country Airplay late in the year.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/david-nail/chart-history/csa/ | title=Country Airplay chart history for David Nail | publisher=Billboard | access-date=October 20, 2021}}</ref>\n\n===2018\u20132022: ''Port Saint Joe'' and ''Skeletons''===\nIn early 2018, the brothers announced the release of their second studio record titled ''[[Port Saint Joe (album)|Port Saint Joe]].'' The album was named for the town of the [[Port St. Joe, Florida|same name]], which was also where the duo recorded it.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Stefano |first1=Angela |title=Brothers Osborne Announce Sophomore Album, 'Port Saint Joe' |url=https://theboot.com/brothers-osborne-port-saint-joe/ |website=The Boot |date=January 24, 2018 |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref> Its lead single was the song \"[[Shoot Me Straight]]\".<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Freeman |first1=Jon |title=Brothers Osborne Announce New Album 'Port Saint Joe' |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/brothers-osborne-announce-new-album-port-saint-joe-197353/ |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=January 24, 2018 |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref> It later reached the top 30 of the ''Billboard'' country songs chart.<ref>{{cite magazine |title=\"Shoot Me Straight\" chart history (Country Songs) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/csi/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref> ''Port Saint Joe'' was officially released in April 2018 via EMI Nashville. Like its predecessor, ''Port Saint Joe'' was produced by Jay Joyce.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> It peaked at number two on the ''Billboard'' country albums list and number 15 on the Billboard 200.<ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Port Saint Joe'' chart history (Country Albums) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/clp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Port Saint Joe'' chart history (Billboard 200) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/tlp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref> Joseph Hudak of ''Rolling Stone'' described the record as \"a concise, 10-song effort.\"<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Hudak |first1=Joseph |title=Why Brothers Osborne Are Country Music's New Working-Class Heroes |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/why-brothers-osborne-are-country-musics-new-working-class-heroes-629723/ |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=April 18, 2018 |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref> Allmusic's Stephen Thomas Erlewine called it a \"clever, smart, adventurous, and hooky, creating a slow-rolling good-time vibe that doesn't lose its luster with repeated plays.\"<ref>{{cite web |last1=Erlewine |first1=Stephen Thomas |title=''Port Saint Joe'': Brothers Osborne: Songs, reviews, credits |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/port-saint-joe-mw0003149739 |website=[[Allmusic]] |access-date=March 8, 2021}}</ref>\n\nBetween 2018 and 2019, the brothers were part of several collaborative projects. In mid-2018, they were featured on [[Dierks Bentley]]'s \"[[Burning Man (song)|Burning Man]]\", a single from his studio album ''[[The Mountain (Dierks Bentley album)|The Mountain]]''.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/dierks-bentley-brothers-osborne-burning-man/|title=Dierks Bentley's 'Burning Man', Featuring Brothers Osborne, Is His Next Single [Listen]|last=Stecker|first=Liv|date=June 25, 2018|work=The Boot|access-date=June 28, 2018}}</ref> The song became their biggest hit since \"Stay a Little Longer\", climbing to the top five of the ''Billboard'' country songs chart.<ref>{{cite magazine |title=\"Burning Man\" chart history |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/csi/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 12, 2021}}</ref> In 2019, the duo collaborated with [[Maren Morris]] on a duet for her studio album ''[[Girl (Maren Morris album)|Girl]]''.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/girl-mw0003252614 | title=''GIRL'' | publisher=AllMusic | access-date=July 23, 2020 | author=Stephen Thomas Erlewine}}</ref> They also joined [[Brooks & Dunn]] on their 2019 album ''[[Reboot (Brooks & Dunn album)|Reboot]]'', where they contributed to a re-recording of that duo's 1993 hit \"[[Hard Workin' Man (song)|Hard Workin' Man]]\".<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/reboot-mw0003255781 | title=''Reboot'' | publisher=AllMusic | access-date=July 23, 2020 | author=Stephen Thomas Erlewine}}</ref> Brothers Osborne were later nominated by the [[Country Music Association]] for their recent collaborative projects.<ref name=\"CMA\">{{cite web |title=CMA Awards Past Winners & Nominees: Brothers Osborne |url=https://cmaawards.com/past-winners-and-nominees/?appSession=876879R7539U1Y1X68JZ153LD56M9PYUFF02CW81HA411B66BC0AG9PEA0CT051A21W8Z00MHVYM95MV8ID2P3ENOU0WZVL1NES0W56GY457M6CV7483625K54E5DIXI |website=[[Country Music Association]] |access-date=March 7, 2021}}</ref> In spring of 2019 The Brothers Osborne were featured guests on the PBS concert series ''Bluegrass Underground'' (now re-branded as ''The Caverns Sessions'').\n\nIn October 2019, they released a live album recorded during three concerts at the [[Ryman Auditorium]] in Nashville.<ref name=\"ryman live\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/brothers-osborne-live-at-the-ryman-album-870363/|title=Brothers Osborne Ready 'Live at the Ryman' Concert Album|first= Joseph|last= Hudak |magazine=Rolling Stone |date=August 12, 2019 }}</ref> This was followed in July 2020 by the announcement of a third studio album, titled ''[[Skeletons (Brothers Osborne album)|Skeletons]]'', which later was later released in October 2020. Also produced by Jay Joyce, the album included songs written by the brothers, with several Nashville songwriters.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/brothers-osborne-new-album-skeletons-1032362/ | title=Brothers Osborne Detail New Album 'Skeletons' | work=Rolling Stone Country | date=July 22, 2020 | access-date=July 23, 2020 | author=Jon Freeman}}</ref> ''Skeletons'' debuted in the top five of the country albums chart and the top 50 on the Billboard 200.<ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Skeletons'' chart history (Country Albums) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/clp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 12, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |title=''Skeletons'' chart history (Billboard 200) |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/tlp/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 12, 2021}}</ref> The album's first charted single is \"[[All Night (Brothers Osborne song)|All Night]].\"<ref>{{cite magazine |title=\"All Night\" chart history |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/brothers-osborne/chart-history/csi/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=March 1, 2021}}</ref> ''Skeletons'' received a favorable response from Allmusic's Stephen Thomas Erlewine, who rated the project four and half stars. Erlewine praised the duo's mixing of different styles and recognized that the brothers had become \"comfortable in the skin.\" Erlewine concluded by saying, \"...the great thing about Skeletons is how it sounds like they're appealing to wide quadrants of rock, pop, country, and Americana audiences without sounding like anything but themselves.\"<ref>{{cite web |last1=Erlewine |first1=Stephen Thomas |title=''Skeletons'': Brothers Osborne: Songs, reviews, credits |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/skeletons-mw0003411938 |website=[[Allmusic]] |access-date=March 12, 2021}}</ref> Jonathan Bernstein of ''Rolling Stone'' rated ''Skeletons'' at three and a half stars. Bernstein commented that the record is \"a remarkably engaging country-leaning rock record that shows off what the duo does best.\"<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Bernstein |first1=Jonathan |title=Brothers Osborne Deliver Their First Full-Fledged Rock Record with 'Skeletons' |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-album-reviews/brothers-osborne-skeletons-1073347/ |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=October 9, 2020 |access-date=March 12, 2021}}</ref>\n\nAt the end of 2021, the duo announced that they would be re-releasing ''Skeletons'' in 2022 with three additional songs. The first of these is \"[[Younger Me]]\", a song released as a promotional single earlier in 2021. This song was also nominated that year for [[Grammy Award for Best Country Duo/Group Performance]]. Also included are \"Headstone\" and \"Midnight Rider's Prayer\", the latter of which incorporates elements of [[Willie Nelson]]'s \"[[On the Road Again (Willie Nelson song)|On the Road Again]]\".<ref name=\"skeletons bonus\">{{cite web | url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/brothers-osborne-skeletons-deluxe-1274135/ | title=Brothers Osborne Revamp 'Skeletons' Album With 'Younger Me,' Bonus Tracks | publisher=Rolling Stone Country | date=December 20, 2021 | accessdate=December 28, 2021}}</ref> In November 2022, Brothers Osborne and [[The War and Treaty]] covered [[The Rolling Stones]]' \"[[It's Only Rock 'n Roll (But I Like It)]]\" on the [[Country Music Association]] awards.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/cma-awards-brothers-osborne-war-and-treaty-1234627204/ | title=The War & Treaty and Brothers Osborne Cover a Rolling Stones Classic at the CMA Awards | publisher=Rolling Stone | date=November 9, 2022 | accessdate=November 14, 2022}}</ref> Brothers Osborne provided backing vocals to [[Ashley McBryde]]'s 2022 album ''[[Lindeville]]'', on which John also served as producer.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/ashley-mcbryde-lindeville-new-album-interview-1235147303/ | title=Ashley McBryde on Crafting 'Lindeville' With Brandy Clark, John Osborne & More: 'It Was Like a Puzzle, Only the Pieces Were Invisible' | publisher=Billboard | date=September 29, 2022 | accessdate=March 31, 2023 | author=Jessica Nicholson}}</ref>\n\n===2023\u2013present: ''Brothers Osborne'' and ''Break Mine''===\nThe duo released three new songs in March 2023: \"[[Nobody's Nobody]]\", \"Might as Well Be Me\", and \"Roller Coaster (Forever and a Day)\".<ref>{{cite web | url=https://holler.country/news/breaking/brothers-osborne-new-album-2023-release-date-and-tracklist | title=Brothers Osborne new album 2023: Release date and track list | publisher=Holler Country | date=March 24, 2023 | accessdate=March 31, 2023}}</ref> The first of these was sent to radio as a single that same month, debuting at number 37 on Country Airplay.<ref>{{cite magazine | url=http://s3.amazonaws.com/bulletins.billboard.com/country/country_update_2023_0414.pdf | title=Billboard Country Update | publisher=April 14, 2023 | magazine=Billboard | accessdate=April 19, 2023}}</ref> On July 14, 2023, the brothers released the song \"Sun Ain't Even Gone Down Yet\" and announced that their upcoming [[Brothers Osborne (album)|self-titled fourth album]] would be released on September 15, 2023.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/brothers-osborne-fourth-studio-album-self-titled|title=Brothers Osborne Reveal Self-Titled Fourth Studio Album, Drops New Song|author=Sterling Whitaker|publisher=Taste of Country|date=July 14, 2023|access-date=July 14, 2023}}</ref> Unlike their previous albums, ''Brothers Osborne'' was produced by [[Mike Elizondo]].<ref name=\"cbs\">{{cite web | url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/brothers-osborne-fourth-album-country-music-journey/ | title=Brothers Osborne say fourth album marks a \"fresh start\" in their country music journey: \"We've shared so much\" | publisher=[[CBS News]] | date=October 3, 2023 | accessdate=December 27, 2023 | author=Anthony Mason, Analisa Novak}}</ref>\n\nOn February 29, 2024, the duo announced that their second EP ''Break Mine'' will be released on March 22, 2024.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://musicrow.com/2024/02/brothers-osborne-to-release-break-mine-ep-in-march |title=Brothers Osborne to Release 'Break Mine' EP in March |author=Lorie Hollabaugh |publisher=Music Row |date=February 29, 2024 |access-date=March 5, 2024}}</ref>\n\n==Musical stylings==\nJohn Osborne is the main instrumentalist of the group, playing primarily [[electric guitar]], while TJ is the lead vocalist. Of their sound, ''[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]'' writer Andrew Unterberger said, \"John's guitar slides a [[Hattori Hanz\u014d]] sharpness, while TJ\u2019s vocals are wisely kept from going too thick with warbling vibrato, allowing them an understated vulnerability badly lacking in Nashville these days.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.spin.com/2016/01/review-brothers-osborne-pawn-shop/|title=Review: Brothers Osborne Take Country to the 'Pawn Shop,' Leave With Something New|last=Unterberger|first=Andrew|date=January 11, 2016|work=Spin|access-date=August 20, 2018}}</ref> [[Stephen Thomas Erlewine]] contrasted the duo with [[Sam Hunt]] and [[Chris Stapleton]], saying that they have \"the modern rhythmic snap of the former and the classicist structure of the latter.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/pawn-shop-mw0002902920|title=''Pawn Shop''|last=Erlewine|first=Stephen Thomas|work=Allmusic|access-date=August 20, 2018}}</ref> Allmusic describes the duo as recording \"earthy, passionate country-rock\",<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> while ''[[Country Standard Time]]'' reviewer Jeffrey B. Remz noted influences of [[outlaw country]] and [[Southern rock]] in ''Pawn Shop''. He also compared TJ's \"sonorous, ultra-deep voice\" favorably to [[Trace Adkins]] and noting the variety of guitar styles played by John as \"sometimes steely, sometimes twangy, sometimes rocking\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/cdreview.asp?xid=5902|title=''Pawn Shop'' review|last=Remz|first=Jeffrey B.|work=[[Country Standard Time]]|access-date=August 20, 2018}}</ref>\n\nWhen asked to name the ten albums that were the biggest influences on his musical life, John Osborne selected releases by [[Darrell Scott]], [[Patty Loveless]], [[Lucinda Williams]], [[Merle Haggard]], [[Willie Nelson]], [[Alan Jackson]], [[Dwight Yoakam]], [[The Chicks]], [[Alison Krauss & Union Station]], and [[Lee Ann Womack]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://consequence.net/2023/09/brothers-osborne-country-albums-crate-digging/5/|title=10 Country Albums John of Brothers Osborne Thinks Everyone Should Own|last=Siroky|first=Mary|work=[[Consequence (publication)|Consequence]]|date=September 12, 2023 |access-date=September 12, 2023}}</ref>\n\n== Personal lives ==\n[[File:Lucie Silvas in Utrecht 2006.jpg|upright|thumb|right|John Osborne has been married to [[Lucie Silvas]] since 2015.|alt=An imge of British singer Lucie Silvas.]]\nJohn Osborne is married to British singer-songwriter [[Lucie Silvas]]. The two met in 2007 during a songwriting session, and married in 2015.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://theboot.com/john-osborne-lucie-silvas-married/ | title=John Osborne + Lucie Silvas \u2014 Country's Greatest Love Stories | publisher=The Boot | date=June 1, 2020 | access-date=February 5, 2020 | author=Annie Zaleski}}</ref> That same year, John played guitar on and co-produced Silvas' studio album ''[[Letters to Ghosts]]''.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/letters-to-ghosts-mw0002869717/credits | title=''Letters to Ghosts'' credits | publisher=AllMusic | access-date=February 5, 2021}}</ref> The couple became parents to boy-and-girl twins in March 2023.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://tasteofcountry.com/brothers-osborne-baby-twins-john-osborne-lucie-silvas/ | title=JUST IN: Brothers Osborne's John Osborne Welcomes Twins with Wife Lucie Silvas | date=March 21, 2023 }}</ref>\n\nOn February 3, 2021, TJ [[Coming out|came out]] as [[homosexuality|gay]], making him the first openly gay artist signed to a major country music label.<ref name=\"CMT-LGBT\">{{cite web |last1=Dowling |first1=Marcus |title=Brothers Osborne's TJ Osborne Is the Only Openly Gay Artist Signed to a Major Country Label |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1829865/brothers-osborne-tj-osborne-only-openly-gay-artist-signed-to-major-country-label/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210209190823/http://www.cmt.com/news/1829865/brothers-osborne-tj-osborne-only-openly-gay-artist-signed-to-major-country-label/ |url-status=dead |archive-date=February 9, 2021 |website=Country Music Television |access-date=February 3, 2021 |date=February 3, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/9520929/brothers-osborne-tj-osborne-comes-out-country-reaction|title=Brothers Osborne's TJ Osborne Gets Love From Dan + Shay, Kacey Musgraves & More After Coming Out|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> The duo's song \"[[Younger Me]]\" was directly inspired by TJ's attempts to come out earlier in his life.<ref name=\"skeletons bonus\"/>\n\nIn 2019, Brothers Osborne canceled a number of tours due to then-undisclosed reasons. In 2021, the duo revealed that this was due to John suffering from [[anxiety disorder]] and [[Major depressive disorder|clinical depression]]. These factors caused [[tinnitus]] and caused him to cancel several recording sessions for ''Skeletons'', and John later stated he considered quitting music entirely as a result.<ref name=\"cbs\"/><ref name=\"considered\">{{cite web | url=https://people.com/country/john-osborne-considered-quitting-music-struggle-anxiety-depression/ | title=John Osborne Says He 'Considered Quitting Music' Due to Struggle with Anxiety and Depression | publisher=[[People (magazine)|People]] | date=April 16, 2021 | accessdate=December 27, 2023}}</ref> A year later, John stated that he was undergoing therapy and medication to treat the disorder.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://people.com/country/john-osborne-not-ashamed-need-help-anxiety-depression/ | title=John Osborne Says He's 'Not Ashamed' to 'Need Help' for His Anxiety and Depression | publisher=People | date=January 21, 2022 | accessdate=December 27, 2023}}</ref>\n\n==Band members==\n'''Current members'''\n* TJ Osborne (born November 18, 1984)<ref name=\"birthdays\">{{cite web | url=https://www.nashcountrydaily.com/birthdays/ | title=Birthdays | work=Nash Country Daily | access-date=April 28, 2020}}</ref> \u2013 lead vocals, rhythm guitar\n* John Osborne (born April 27, 1982)<ref name=\"birthdays\"/> \u2013 lead guitar, backing vocals\n\n'''Touring members'''<ref>{{cite web|url=http://nysmusic.com/2015/05/14/brothers-osborne-rock-the-small-but-mighty-crowd-at-kegs-canalside/|title=Brothers Osborne Rock The \"Small But Mighty Crowd\" at Kegs Canalside \u2013 NYS Music|first=Kathy|last=Stockbridge|website=nysmusic.com|date=May 14, 2015 }}</ref>\n* [[Adam Box]] \u2013 drums, percussion\n* Jason Graumlich \u2013 electric guitar, acoustic guitar, mandolin, backing vocals\n* Billy Justineau (former) - keyboards\n* Pete Sternberg \u2013 bass guitar\n* Dane Farnsworth - keyboards, organ\n* Preston Wait - acoustic guitar, fiddle, steel guitar\n\n== Discography ==\n{{main|Brothers Osborne discography}}\n\n;Studio albums\n*''[[Pawn Shop (album)|Pawn Shop]]'' (2016)\n*''[[Port Saint Joe (album)|Port Saint Joe]]'' (2018)\n*''[[Skeletons (Brothers Osborne album)|Skeletons]]'' (2020)\n*''[[Brothers Osborne (album)|Brothers Osborne]]'' (2023)\n\n==Television appearances==\n{| class=\"wikitable\" style=\"text-align:center;\" \n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"McGuffey_Lane","to":"McGuffey Lane"}],"pages":{"18776139":{"pageid":18776139,"ns":0,"title":"McGuffey Lane","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Refimprove|date=September 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = McGuffey Lane\n| image                 =\n| caption            =\n| image_size            =\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Athens, Ohio]], United States\n| genre               = [[Country rock]]\n| years_active        = 1972\u2013present\n| label               = Atco<br/>[[Atlantic Records|Atlantic]]<br/>HCH\nLick\n| current_members     = Terry Efaw<br/>Steve Reis<br/> John Schwab<br/>Randy Huff<br/>Molly Pauken<br/>Kevin Reed\n| past_members        = Joe Pate<br/>Bobby Gene McNelley<br/>Tebes Douglass\n| associated_acts     =\n}}\n\n'''McGuffey Lane''' is an American [[country rock]] band from [[Athens, Ohio]], and/or [[Columbus, Ohio]], United States. The group was formed in 1972 by Terry Efaw and Steve Reis, who played together under the name Scotch & Soda. After adding songwriter, lead singer, and guitarist Bobby E. McNelley, they branded themselves McGuffey Lane, the location of Reis's [[Athens, Ohio]], home.\n\nThe band eventually expanded to a sextet and became well-known locally, releasing their first album on their own Paradise Island record label. The [[LP record|LP]] sold more than 40,000 copies,<ref name=amg>{{cite web|author=Sandra Brennan |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/mcguffey-lane-mn0000397192/biography |title=McGuffey Lane &#124; Biography & History |website=[[AllMusic]] |date= |accessdate=2020-04-11}}</ref> and eventually resulted in their signing with [[Atco Records]]. They reissued the debut in 1980 and toured with the [[Charlie Daniels Band]], [[The Judds]], and the [[Allman Brothers Band]]. The follow-up, ''Aqua Dream'', featured the single \"Start It All Over\", which spent three weeks on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]], peaking at number 97 in February 1982.<ref name=\"Hot 100 chart history\">{{Cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/mcguffey-lane |title=McGuffey Lane &#124; Billboard |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=2019-02-22 |archive-date=2019-02-23 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190223094337/https://www.billboard.com/music/mcguffey-lane |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\nThe group scored several minor hits on the country charts, but their label wanted to market them more as a pop-country act in the vein of [[Alabama (American band)|Alabama]]. They moved to [[Atlantic Records]] to focus more on country chart success, but as they prepared 1984's ''Day By Day'', keyboardist Tebes Douglass was killed in a [[car crash]]. Soon after, Bobby Gene McNelley left the group to pursue a solo career as a songwriter in [[Nashville, Tennessee]]. In 1985, McGuffey Lane was dropped from Atlantic. In 1986, they released a [[Christmas]] album in support of the Central Ohio Lung Association; toward the end of that year, they inked a sponsorship with [[Miller Beer]], but a planned comeback fizzled.\n\nThe group played into the late 1980s but had dissolved by 1990. In 1995, they reunited after releasing a greatest hits album, and continued performing locally in Ohio into the 2000s. Two full-length releases followed the reunion, in 1998 and 2002. On August 18, 2009,  they opened for [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]] at [[Lifestyle Communities Pavilion|The LC]] in Columbus, Ohio. In March 2010, Lick Records signed a distribution deal with E1 Entertainment, which allows the new McGuffey Lane album to be sold in [[Wal-Mart]] and [[Best Buy]].\n\n==Zachariah's Red Eye Reunion==\nEvery January, McGuffey Lane holds an annual reunion concert featuring many acts who also played at Zachariah's Red Eye Saloon. The first two reunions were held at Villa Milano Banquet and Conference Center, located on Schrock Road on the northeast side of Columbus, Ohio. After the initial two events, John Schwab (who is the organizer of the event) started looking for a larger venue to host the reunion concert, as it had outgrown Villa Milano. He settled on Lifestyles Communities Pavilion (now [[KEMBA Live!]]). The 2013 Reunion currently holds the indoor attendance record at the LC. The fourteenth anniversary took place on January 25, 2014.\n\nSome acts who have taken part in the event are: Rob McNelly (son of original lead singer Bobby Gene McNelly and current guitarist for [[Bob Seger and The Silver Bullet Band]]), John David Call (steel guitarist for [[Pure Prairie League]]), Steve Smith, Gary Ballen, Delyn Christian, Tom Ingham, the Dan Orr Project, Cliff Cody, Grassanine, and [[Erica Blinn]].\n\n==Members==\n*Terry Efaw \u2013 Steel guitar, gutstring guitar, electric guitar\n*Steve Reis \u2013 Bass, vocals\n*Molly Pauken- Mandolin, acoustic guitar, This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Reckless_Kelly_(band)","to":"Reckless Kelly (band)"}],"pages":{"13473822":{"pageid":13473822,"ns":0,"title":"Reckless Kelly (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{copyvio-revdel|url=https://recklesskelly.com/pages/about|start1=1236662505|end1=1247714206}}\n{{Short description|American band}}\n{{Multiple issues|\n{{More footnotes needed|date=May 2010}}\n{{More citations needed|date=September 2011}}}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Reckless Kelly\n| image               =Reckless Kelly (1).jpg\n| caption             =Willy Braun and Chris Schelske at the Reckless Kelly Celebrity Softball Jam\n| image_size          =\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Stanley, Idaho]], U.S.\n| genre               = {{Flatlist|\n* [[Country rock]]\n}}\n| years_active        = 1997-present.\n| label               =\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             = [http://www.recklesskelly.com/ www.recklesskelly.com]\n| current_members     = Willy Braun<br />Cody Braun<br />Ryan Engleman<br />Jay Nazz<br />Joe Miller\n| past_members        = David Abeyta<br />Casey Pollock<br />Adam Odor<br />Jimmy \"JAM\" McFeeley<br />Chris Schelske\n}}\n\n'''Reckless Kelly''' is an American [[country rock]] band formed in [[Stanley, Idaho]]. The band relocated to [[Austin, Texas]] in October 1996.\n\n==History==\nLed by brothers Willy (vocals/guitar) and Cody Braun (vocals/fiddle/mandolin/harmonica), the alternative country-rock outfit Reckless Kelly formed in Stanley, Idaho in February 1996 before moving to Austin, Texas. The Brauns had previously toured with their father in Muzzie Braun & the Boys, a Western swing band, and were joined in their own group by the lead guitarist Casey Pollock, the bass guitarist Chris Schelske and the drummer Jay Nazz.\n\nWith their younger brothers Micky and Gary, Cody and Willy were raised in [[central Idaho]] near the [[Sawtooth Range (Idaho)|Sawtooth Mountains]], between [[Clayton, Idaho|Clayton]] and [[Challis, Idaho|Challis]] in [[Custer County, Idaho|Custer County]], and were homeschooled by their mother. Originally they were \"Muzzie Braun & the Little Braun Brothers\", as Muzzie and his brothers Gary and Billy were the \"Braun Brothers\" from [[Twin Falls, Idaho|Twin Falls]] in the 1970s and early 1980s, sons of the musician Eustaceus \"Mustie\" Braun.<ref name=bbhra>{{cite news |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=eJVfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=JDEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3614%2C1990319 |work=Lewiston Morning Tribune |location=(Idaho)|last=McCarthy |first=John |title=Braun Brothers hit the road again for tour |date=June 22, 1990 |page=1D}}</ref><ref name=lntobitmmb81>{{cite news |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=tJxfAAAAIBAJ&sjid=tjEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=5698%2C1808942 |work=Lewiston Morning Tribune |location=(Idaho) |agency=(obituary) |title=Mustie and Marian Braun, former Lewiston residents |date=February 20, 1981 |page=5C}}</ref> From [[North Dakota]], Mustie was a neighbor and relative of the bandleader [[Lawrence Welk]], and was a keyboard player during the last days of legalized gambling in Idaho at [[Weiser, Idaho|Weiser]] in the early 1950s. He then moved to the new Club [[U.S. Route 93|93]] in [[Jackpot, Nevada]], on the Idaho border, and moved his family to Twin Falls, about fifty miles (80&nbsp;km) north.<ref name=tmbfipt>{{cite news |url=http://www.idahopress.com/cavalcade/the-musical-braun-family/article_8d62e3c2-5703-11e0-9cb7-001cc4c03286.html |work=Idaho Press-Tribune |location=(Nampa)|last=Lea|first=Dan|title=The musical Braun family|date=April 2, 2011 |accessdate=March 20, 2017}}</ref> In February 1981, Mustie and wife Marian (''[[n\u00e9e]]'' Beckman) were involved in a [[head-on collision]] north of Jackpot, and both died from their injuries.<ref name=lntobitmmb81/>\n\nIn 1989, Muzzie and his sons appeared on [[Johnny Carson]]'s ''[[The Tonight Show Starring Johnny Carson|Tonight Show]]'' twice.<ref name=bbhra/><ref name=tmbfipt/>\n\nReckless Kelly played locally on the historic Sixth Street in Austin. They turned Lucy's Retired Surfers Bar, a small bar and restaurant, into a noted music venue with their Monday night residency from November 1996 to May 1998. During this period, other music venues in Austin invited them to play, including the Continental Club, the Saxon Pub, [[Stubb's Bar-B-Q|Stubb's Barbecue]], and Antone's Home of the Blues.\n\nReckless Kelly's first album, ''[[Millican (album)|Millican]]'', appeared in fall 1997 and was officially released in 1998. ''[[Acoustic: Live at Stubb's]]'' and ''[[The Day (Reckless Kelly album)|The Day]]'' followed two years later, after which David Abeyta replaced Pollock on lead guitar. ''[[Under the Table and Above the Sun|Under the Table & Above the Sun]]'' in 2003 began the band's relationship with the high-profile Sugar Hill label and won the hearts of the music press and the honky tonkin' legend [[Joe Ely]], who sang the band's praises in interviews. ''[[Wicked Twisted Road]]'' was released in 2005, and the next year the live album ''[[Reckless Kelly Was Here]]'' captured the band's stage presence. ''[[Bulletproof (Reckless Kelly album)|Bulletproof]]'' was released in summer 2008 on a new label, [[Yep Roc Records]], and includes tracks critical of and reflecting on recent sociopolitical unfoldings, such as the [[Iraq War]] and [[Hurricane Katrina]]. In 2010, Reckless released an album of songs by one of their musical heroes, Pinto Bennett. ''[[Somewhere in Time (Reckless Kelly album)|Somewhere in Time]]'', in the band's own words, highlighted their love of \"straight-up honky tonk\". The band regularly returns to Austin to play before capacity crowds at venues like Nutty Brown Cafe & Amphitheatre.\n\nYounger brothers Micky and Gary Braun front their own band, [[Micky & The Motorcars]]. Both bands play at the annual Braun Brothers Reunion in Challis, Idaho, in August.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Title\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Cold_Creek_County","to":"Cold Creek County"}],"pages":{"47505222":{"pageid":47505222,"ns":0,"title":"Cold Creek County","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|Canadian country rock group}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Cold Creek County\n| image           = \n| caption         = \n| image_size      =\n| alias           =\n| origin          = [[Brighton, Ontario]], [[Canada]]\n| genre           = [[Country rock]]\n| years_active    = 2014\u20132019\n| label           = [[Sony Music Canada]]\n| associated_acts =\n| current_members = <br />Brandon Scott\n| past_members    = Brandon Scott (lead singer) <br /> Ches Anthony (lead singer)<br /> Doug Oliver<br />Josh Lester (guitar/vocals)<br />Justin Lester(bass/vocals)\n}}\n''' Cold Creek County '''is a Canadian [[country rock]] group based in [[Brighton, Ontario|Brighton]], [[Ontario]]. Its members are Doug Oliver, Josh Lester, Trevor MacLeod, Justin Lester, and Jordan Honsinger. They were founded in 2013<ref>{{cite news|last1=Bencic|first1=Sarah|title=Local Tunes: Cold Creek County|url=http://trentarthur.ca/local-tunes-cold-creek-county/|accessdate=June 28, 2015|work=Arthur|date=January 20, 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=A rocking good time was had by all|url=http://www.insidebelleville.com/whatson-story/4198754-a-rocking-good-time-was-had-by-all/|accessdate=June 28, 2015|work=Inside Belleville|date=November 7, 2013}}</ref> and signed to [[Sony Music Canada]] in 2014.<ref name=\"thatscountry\">{{cite news|title=Cold Creek County's Debut Single \"Our Town\" #1 Most Added \u2013 All Formats|url=http://thatscountry.com/2015/05/14/cold-creek-countys-debut-single-our-town-1-most-added-all-formats/|accessdate=June 28, 2015|work=That's Country|date=May 14, 2015}}</ref><ref name=\"cmt\">{{cite web|title=Cold Creek County Biography|url=http://www.cmt.ca/artist/cold-creek-county|website=[[CMT (Canadian TV channel)|CMT]]|accessdate=June 28, 2015}}</ref>\n\n==History==\n\nThey toured with [[Dallas Smith (singer)|Dallas Smith]], [[Emerson Drive]], [[Kira Isabella]] and [[Jason Blaine]].<ref name=\"cmt\" /> They released their debut single, \"Our Town\", in April 2015.<ref>{{cite news|title=Cold Creek County Releases Debut Single \"Our Town\" Co-Written By Todd Clark|url=http://www.windupsongs.com/cold-creek-county-releases-debut-single-our-town-co-written-by-todd-clark/|accessdate=June 28, 2015|work=Wind-Up Songs|date=April 28, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150630141904/http://www.windupsongs.com/cold-creek-county-releases-debut-single-our-town-co-written-by-todd-clark/|archive-date=June 30, 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref> It was the most added debut single by a Canadian country artist.<ref name=\"thatscountry\" /> It has reached the top 10 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Canada Country]] chart.<ref name=\"Canada Country\">{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/biz/search/charts?f%5B0%5D=ts_chart_artistname%3ACold%20Creek%20County&f%5B1%5D=itm_field_chart_id%3A1240&f%5B2%5D=ss_bb_type%3Achart_item&type=2&artist=Cold%20Creek%20County|title=Cold Creek County Album & Song Chart History - Canada Country|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|publisher=[[Prometheus Global Media]]|accessdate=June 28, 2015}}</ref> It was written by Todd Clark and Gavin Slate.\n\nThe band performed in 2016 at the Tweed Stampede and Jamboree.<ref>[https://www.intelligencer.ca/2016/08/01/photos-rodeo-in-tweed/wcm/c7fc9cb1-5833-b8e9-d965-c056c4142fe4 \"PHOTOS: Rodeo in Tweed\"]. ''The Belleville Intelligencer'', August 1, 2016</ref> That year the band was presented with a Canadian Radio Music Award.<ref>[https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/7357941/crmas-2016-canadian-radio-music-awards-dance-the-weeknd-alessia-cara \"The Weeknd, Alessia Cara & More Score at 2016 Canadian Radio Music Awards\"]. ''BillBoard'', 5/6/2016 by Matt Medved</ref>\n\nIn June, 2019 Cold Creek Country performed at the Country Music Association of Ontario awards gala.<ref>[https://www.fyimusicnews.ca/articles/2019/06/17/meghan-patrick-triumphant-cmaontario-awards \"Meghan Patrick Triumphant At CMAOntario Awards\"]. ''FYI Music News'', Jun 17, 2019.</ref> On September 24, 2019, Josh Lester and his brother Justin left the band.\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center\"\n|-\n!
