Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Hank_Williams_Jr.","to":"Hank Williams Jr."}],"pages":{"168285":{"pageid":168285,"ns":0,"title":"Hank Williams Jr.","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer-songwriter and musician (born 1949)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=April 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Hank Williams Jr.\n| image             = Hank212.JPG\n| caption           = Williams in 2008\n| image_upright     = \n| birth_name        = Randall Hank Williams\n| alias             = {{hlist|Bocephus|Rockin' Randall|Wham Bam Sam|Luke the Drifter Jr.|Thunderhead Hawkins}}\n| birth_date        = {{birth date and age|1949|5|26}}\n| birth_place       = [[Shreveport, Louisiana]], U.S.\n| instrument        = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar|banjo|piano|keyboards|harmonica|fiddle|drums}}\n| genre             = {{Hlist|[[Country rock]]|[[southern rock]]|[[outlaw country]]|[[blues rock]]|[[rock and roll]]}}\n| occupation        = {{hlist|Singer-songwriter|musician}}\n| years_active      = 1963\u2013present\n| label             = {{hlist|[[MGM Records|MGM]]|[[Warner Records|Warner Bros.]]|[[Curb Records|Curb]]|Bocephus|NASH Icon}}\n| spouse            = {{marriage|Gwen Yeargin|1971|1977|reason=divorce}} {{marriage|Becky White|1977|1983|reason=divorce}} {{marriage|Mary Jane Thomas|1990|2022|reason=died}} {{marriage|Brandi Williams|2023}}{{efn|group=brandi|Brandi's last name is currently unknown.}}\n| website           = {{URL|hankjr.com}}\n| module            = {{Infobox person|child=yes\n| children = 5, including [[Hank Williams III]] and [[Holly Williams (musician)|Holly Williams]]\n}}\n}}\n\n'''Randall Hank Williams''' (born May 26, 1949), known professionally as '''Hank Williams Jr.''' or '''Bocephus''', is an American singer-songwriter and musician. His musical style has been described as a blend of [[rock music|rock]], [[blues]], and [[country music|country]]. He is the son of country musician [[Hank Williams]] and the father of musicians [[Holly Williams (musician)|Holly Williams]] and [[Hank Williams III]], and the grandfather of [[Coleman Williams]]. He is also the half brother of [[Jett Williams]].\n\nWilliams began his career following in his famed father's footsteps, covering his father's songs and imitating his father's style. Williams' first television appearance was in a December 1963 episode of ''[[The Ed Sullivan Show]]'', in which at age fourteen he sang several songs associated with his father. Later that year, he was a guest star on ''[[Shindig!]]''<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.imdb.com/name/nm0929947/?ref_=ttfc_fc_cl_t130|title=Hank Williams, Jr.|publisher=[[IMDb]]|access-date=August 8, 2018}}</ref>\n\nAs Williams struggled to define his own voice and place within the [[country music]] genre, his style began slowly to evolve. His career was interrupted by a near-fatal fall while Williams was climbing [[List of mountains in Beaverhead County, Montana|Ajax Peak in Montana]] on August 8, 1975.<ref name=\"People\">{{cite journal|last=Buchalter|first=Gail|date=October 22, 1979|title=Hank Williams Jr. Fell Down a Mountain and Lived Now He's Climbing High on the C&w Charts|journal=[[People (magazine)|People]]|volume=12|issue=17|url=http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0,,20074883,00.html|access-date=August 3, 2013|archive-date=April 25, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160425141320/http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0,,20074883,00.html|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=\"TheFall\">{{cite web|url=http://countrymusichalloffame.org/the-fall/|title=The Fall|publisher=[[Country Music Hall of Fame]]|access-date=August 3, 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101104074223/http://countrymusichalloffame.org/the-fall/|archive-date=November 4, 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref> After an extended recovery, he rebuilt his career in the [[country rock]] scene.<ref name=Burns/> As a multi-instrumentalist, Williams' repertoire of musical instrument skills includes guitar, bass guitar, [[upright bass]], [[steel guitar]], [[banjo]], [[dobro]], piano, keyboards, saxophone, [[harmonica]], [[fiddle]], and drums.<ref name=\"autogenerated1\">{{Cite web|url=http://www.hankjr.com/about/?id=2|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110716224600/http://www.hankjr.com/about/?id=2|url-status=dead|title=Hank Williams Jr. \u2013 Official Website|archive-date=July 16, 2011|access-date=November 5, 2020}}</ref> In 2020, Williams Jr. was inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum|Country Music Hall of Fame]].<ref name=\"Paulson\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/2020/08/12/hank-williams-jr-marty-stuart-dean-dillon-country-music-hall-fame/3352839001/|title=Hank Williams Jr., Marty Stuart, Dean Dillon to enter the Country Music Hall of Fame|first=Matthew Leimkuehler and Dave|last=Paulson|newspaper=[[The Tennessean]]|access-date=November 5, 2020}}</ref>\n\n==Early life==\nWilliams was born Randall Hank Williams on May 26, 1949, in [[Shreveport, Louisiana]]. His [[Hank Williams|father]] nicknamed him Bocephus (after [[Grand Ole Opry]] comedian [[Rod Brasfield]]'s ventriloquist dummy).<ref>{{cite magazine|url =https://www.newyorker.com/culture/culture-desk/the-awkward-enduring-influence-of-hank-williams-jr|title =The Awkward, Enduring Influence of Hank Williams, Jr.|magazine =The New Yorker|first =David|last =Cantwell|date =March 24, 2016}}</ref> After his father's death in 1953, he was raised by his mother, [[Audrey Williams]].\n\nWhile he was a child, Williams was influenced by a <!--really? vast--> number of contemporary musicians who visited his family and taught him various musical instruments and styles. {{citation needed|date=June 2020}} Among these figures of influence were [[Merle Haggard]], [[Johnny Cash]], [[Fats Domino]], [[Earl Scruggs]], [[Lightnin' Hopkins]], and [[Jerry Lee Lewis]]. Williams first stepped onto the stage and sang his father's songs when he was eight years old.\n\nHe attended [[John Overton High School]] in [[Nashville, Tennessee]], where he would bring his guitar to music class and play for pep rallies and performances with the choir.\n\n== Career ==\nIn 1964, Williams made his recording debut with \"[[Long Gone Lonesome Blues]]\", one of his father's many classic songs.<ref>{{cite book |title=The Billboard Book Of Top 40 Country Hits: 1944\u20132006, Second edition |last=Whitburn |first=Joel |year=2004 |publisher=Record Research |page=388 |language=en |isbn=0823082911 }}</ref>\n\nHe provided the singing voice of his father<ref name=\"pc9\">{{Pop Chronicles |9 |4|Hank Williams Jr.}}</ref> in the 1964 film ''[[Your Cheatin' Heart (film)|Your Cheatin' Heart]].''<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0058765/ |title=Your Cheatin' Heart |date=December 1, 1964 |website=IMDb.com}}</ref> He also recorded an album of duets with recordings of his father.<ref name=\"pc9\" />\n\n===A change in appearance and musical direction===\nAlthough Williams' recordings earned him numerous country hits throughout the 1960s and early 1970s with his role as a \"Hank Williams impersonator\", he became disillusioned and severed ties with his mother.\n\nBy the mid-1970s Williams began to pursue a musical direction that would eventually make him a superstar. While recording a series of moderately successful songs, Williams began a pattern of heavy drug and alcohol abuse. Upon moving to [[Alabama]], in an attempt to refocus both his creative energy and his troubled personal life, Williams began playing music with [[Southern rock]] musicians including [[Waylon Jennings]], [[Toy Caldwell]], and [[Charlie Daniels]]. ''[[Hank Williams Jr. and Friends]]'' (1975), often considered his watershed album, was the product of these then-groundbreaking collaborations.\n\nOn August 8, 1975, Williams was nearly killed while mountain climbing in southwestern [[Montana]]. While climbing [[List of mountains in Beaverhead County, Montana|Ajax Peak]] on the [[Continental Divide of the Americas|continental divide]] ([[Idaho]] border) west of [[Jackson, Montana|Jackson]], the snow beneath Williams collapsed and he fell almost {{convert|500|ft}} onto rock, causing multiple severe skull and facial fractures.<ref name=singfll>{{cite news |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=8R9OAAAAIBAJ&pg=1923%2C4536621 |work=Spokesman-Review |location=(Spokane, Washington) |agency=Associated Press |title=Singer injured in fall |date=August 11, 1975 |page=1}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| url=https://www.usatoday.com/life/people/2006-01-11-williams-miner-visit_x.htm?POE=LIFISVA | work=USA Today | title=Hank Williams visits W.Va. mine survivor | date=January 11, 2006}}</ref> Williams spent two years recovering, re-learning how to talk and sing, and undergoing 17 surgeries to repair his skull and reconstruct his face. The accident was chronicled in the semi-autobiographical, made-for-television film ''[[Living Proof: The Hank Williams Jr. Story]]''. To hide his scars and disfigurement from the accident, Williams grew a beard and began wearing sunglasses and a [[cowboy hat]]. The beard, hat, and sunglasses have since become Williams' [[trademark look|signature look]].{{citation needed|date=December 2022}}\n\nIn 1977, Williams recorded and released ''One Night Stands'' and ''The New South'', and worked closely with his old friend Waylon Jennings on the song \"Once and For All\".{{citation needed|date=December 2022}} In 1980, he appeared on the [[PBS]] show ''[[Austin City Limits]]'' during Season 5, along with the Shake Russell-[[Dana Cooper]] Band.{{citation needed|date=December 2022}}\n\n===Country music career===\n{{BLP sources section|date=October 2008}}\n[[File:HankWilliamsJrCollage-1000.jpg|thumb|upright=1.45|Williams performing at the Chumash Casino Resort in Santa Ynez, California, 2006]]\n\nIn 1976, ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' wrote that Williams' \"mainstream country material has always been among [[Nashville Tennessee|Nashville]]{{'}}s best\".<ref>{{Cite web| title = Hank Williams Jr.: Hank William Jr. and Friends. By John Morthland : Articles, reviews and interviews from Rock's Backpages.| access-date = June 25, 2018| url = https://www.rocksbackpages.com/Library/Article/hank-williams-jr-ihank-william-jr-and-friendsi|via=[[Rock's Backpages]] |url-access=subscription }}</ref>\n\nHe was prolific throughout the 1980s, sometimes recording and releasing two albums a year. ''[[Family Tradition (album)|Family Tradition]]'', ''[[Whiskey Bent and Hell Bound (album)|Whiskey Bent and Hell Bound]]'', ''[[Habits Old and New]]'', ''[[Rowdy (Hank Williams, Jr. album)|Rowdy]]'', ''[[The Pressure Is On]]'', ''[[High Notes]]'', ''[[Strong Stuff]]'', ''[[Man of Steel (album)|Man of Steel]]'', ''[[Major Moves (album)|Major Moves]]'', ''[[Five-O (album)|Five-O]]'', ''[[Montana Cafe]]'', and many others resulted in a long string of hits.\n\nBetween 1979 and 1992, Williams released 21 albums\u201418 studio albums and three compilations\u2014that were all certified at least [[Music recording certification|gold]] by the [[Recording Industry Association of America|RIAA]]. Between 1979 and 1990, he enjoyed a string of 30 Top Ten singles on the Billboard Country charts, including eight No.&nbsp;1 singles, for a total of 44 Top Ten singles, including a total of 10 No.&nbsp;1 singles, during his career.\n\nIn 1982, he had nine albums simultaneously on the Billboard Top Country Albums chart, all of which were original works and not compilations. In 1987\u201388, Williams was named Entertainer of the Year by the [[Country Music Association]]. In 1987, 1988, and 1989, he won the same award from the [[Academy of Country Music]]. The pinnacle album of his acceptance and popularity was ''[[Born to Boogie (album)|Born to Boogie]]''.\n\nDuring the 1980s, Williams Jr. became a country music superstar known for catchy anthems and hard-edged, rock-influenced country. During the late 1970s and into the mid-1980s, Williams' songs constantly flew into the number one or number two spots, with songs such as \"Family Tradition\", \"Whiskey Bent and Hell Bound\", \"Old Habits\", \"Ain't Misbehavin{{'\"}}, \"[[Born to Boogie (song)|Born to Boogie]]\", and \"My Name Is Bocephus\".\n\nThe hit single \"[[Wild Streak]]\" (1987) was co-written by [[Houston]] native [[Terri Sharp]], for which Williams and Sharp both earned gold records. In 1988, he released a Southern pride song, \"[[If the South Woulda Won]]\". The reference is to a notional Southern victory in the [[American Civil War|Civil War]].\n\nHis 1989 hit \"[[There's a Tear in My Beer]]\" was a duet with his father created using electronic merging technology. The song was written by his father, and had been previously recorded with Hank Williams playing the guitar as the sole instrument. The music video for the song combined existing television footage of Hank Williams performing, onto which electronic merging technology impressed the recordings of Williams, which then made it appear as if he were actually playing with his father. The video was both a critical and commercial success. It was named ''Video of the Year'' by both the Country Music Association and the Academy of Country Music. Williams would go on to win a [[Grammy Award]] in 1990 for [[Grammy Award for Best Country Collaboration with Vocals|Best Country Vocal Collaboration]].\n\nHe is well known for his hit \"[[A Country Boy Can Survive]]\" and as the performer of the theme song for ''[[Monday Night Football]]'', based on his 1984 hit \"[[All My Rowdy Friends Are Coming Over Tonight]]\". In 1991, 1992, 1993, and 1994, Williams' opening themes for ''Monday Night Football'' earned him four [[Emmy Award]]s. \n[[File:Hank Williams, Jr. (2006).jpg|thumb|Williams in 2006]]\nIn 2000, he provided the voice of Injun Joe in ''[[Tom Sawyer (2000 film)|Tom Sawyer]]''. In 2001, Williams Jr. co-wrote his classic hit \"A Country Boy Can Survive\" after 9/11, renaming it \"America Can Survive\". In 2004, Williams was featured prominently on ''CMT Outlaws''. In 2006, he starred at the Summerfest concert.\n\nHe has also made a cameo appearance along with [[Larry the Cable Guy]], [[Kid Rock]], and [[Charlie Daniels]] in [[Gretchen Wilson]]'s music video for the song \"[[All Jacked Up (song)|All Jacked Up]]\". He and Kid Rock also appeared in Wilson's \"[[Redneck Woman]]\" video. Hank also had a small part of Kid Rock's video \"Only God Knows Why\", and \"Redneck Paradise\".\n\nIn April 2009, Williams released a new single, \"Red, White & Pink-Slip Blues\", which peaked at number 43 on the country charts. The song was the lead-off single to Williams' album ''[[127 Rose Avenue]]''. The album debuted and peaked at number 7 on the ''Billboard'' Top Country Albums chart. Also in July 2009, ''127 Rose Avenue'' was announced as his last album for Curb Records.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1616664/hank-williams-jr-says-new-album-is-his-last-for-curb-records.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090725202808/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1616664/hank-williams-jr-says-new-album-is-his-last-for-curb-records.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=July 25, 2009|title=Hank Williams Jr. says new album is his last for Curb Records|last=Morris|first=Edward|work=[[Country Music Television]]|date=July 21, 2009|access-date=July 24, 2009}}</ref>\n\n== Musical style ==\nAs a multi-instrumentalist, Williams' repertoire of skills includes guitar, bass guitar, [[upright bass]], [[steel guitar]], [[banjo]], [[Resonator guitar]], piano, keyboards, saxophone, [[harmonica]], [[fiddle]], and drums.<ref name=\"autogenerated1\"/> Williams began his recording career performing covers of his father's songs. Despite catering to the country music market, Williams preferred to listen to [[rhythm and blues]].<ref name=Dukes/> Williams also recorded singles under the name Luke the Drifter Jr.<ref name=Harrington>{{cite news |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/archive/lifestyle/1992/12/16/recordings/72741d15-828d-4c87-a3b0-1893e1a975af/ |title=Recordings |last=Harrington |first=Richard |date=December 16, 1992 |newspaper=The Washington Post |access-date=2022-04-22}}</ref> (a reference to his father's alias \"Luke the Drifter\"), [[rock and roll]] singles under the aliases Rockin' Randall<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/hank-williams-jr-mn0000117844/biography |title=Artist Biography |last=Erlewine |first=Stephen Thomas |publisher=AllMusic |access-date=2022-04-22}}</ref> and Bocephus<ref name=Harrington/> (a nickname given to him by his father), and [[blues]] under the name Thunderhead Hawkins.<ref name=Dukes>{{cite web |url=https://tasteofcountry.com/hank-williams-jr-rich-white-honky-blues-album-title-interview/ |title=Hank Williams Jr. Explains 'Rich White Honky Blues' Album Title |last=Dukes |first=Billy |date=June 17, 2022 |publisher=Taste of Country |access-date=2022-09-08}}</ref> Williams' music has been categorized as [[country rock]],<ref name=Burns>{{cite web |url=https://www.pbs.org/kenburns/country-music/hank-williams-jr-biography|title=Hank Williams Jr. Biography |last=Burns|first=Ken |date= |work=PBS |access-date=2023-07-07 |quote=He began the slow rebuilding of his career, this time entirely in the Southern country-rock genre.}}</ref> [[blues rock]],<ref name=Webb>{{cite web |url=https://amp.oklahoman.com/amp/62781299007 |title=Hank Williams Jr. Rocks Norman Crowd |last=Webb |first=Todd |date=December 7, 1984 |publisher=Oklahoman |access-date=2023-07-07 |quote=Williams returned the welcome with an inspired set of country-style rock 'n' roll at its best. [...] a full-speed-ahead set of no-holds-barred rock, blues-rock, and rockabilly rock so intense that Williams himself was forced to partially disrobe near the end of the show. }}</ref> [[southern rock]],<ref name=Malone>{{cite book |editor-last=Malone |editor-first=Bill |date=February 2014 |title=The New Encyclopedia of Southern Culture|chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=AOynAgAAQBAJ&pg=PA383 |chapter=Williams, Hank Jr. |publisher=University of North Carolina Press |page=383 |isbn=978-1469616667}}</ref> [[outlaw country]],<ref name=Erlewine>{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/hank-williams-jr-mn0000117844/biography |title= Hank Williams, Jr. Biography |last=Erlewine|first=Stephen Thomas |work=AllMusic |access-date=2023-07-07}}</ref> [[rockabilly]]<ref name=Webb/> and [[rock and roll]].<ref name=Webb/>\n\n== Legacy ==\nArtists who have cited Hank Williams Jr. as an influence include Delta Generators,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://amp.telegram.com/amp/63214191007 |title=Country and blues on stage this Friday |last=Banner |first=Sandy Meindersma |date=July 31, 2008 |publisher=Telegram & Gazette |access-date=2022-04-22}}</ref> [[Walker Hayes]],<ref>{{cite web |url=https://tasteofcountry.com/walker-hayes-hank-williams-jr-song-influence-interview/ |title=WALKER HAYES ON HIS LOVE OF HANK JR., DON WILLIAMS |last=Paul |first=Evan |date=January 27, 2022 |publisher=Taste of Country |access-date= |quote=}}</ref> [[Sam Hunt]],<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/country-radio-seminar-closes-with-sam-hunt-frankie-ballard-6487466/ |title=Country Radio Seminar Closes With Stellar Performances by Sam Hunt, Cole Swindell & More |last=Dauphin |first=Chuck |date=February 28, 2015 |website= |publisher=Billboard |access-date=2022-04-22}}</ref> Davin James,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/davin-james-mn0000230651/biography |title=Artist Biography |last=Hage |first=Erik |publisher=AllMusic |access-date=2022-04-22 }}</ref> [[Shooter Jennings]],<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/shooter-jennings-premieres-drunk-talks-hank-williams-jr-influence-8468362/ |title=Shooter Jennings Premieres 'D.R.U.N.K.,' Talks Hank Williams Jr. Influence |last=Dauphin |first=Chuck |date=August 3, 2018 |publisher=Billboard |access-date=2022-04-20}}</ref> [[Wayne Mills (singer)|Wayne Mills]],<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/music/2013/12/17/country-singer-killed/4049361/ |title=Bar owner charged in singer's death released from jail |last=Gonzalez |first=Tony |date=December 17, 2013 |publisher=USA Today |access-date= |quote=}}</ref> The Sickstring Outlaws<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.sandiegoreader.com/news/2019/aug/01/live-five-electric-hoedown-hillbillies-steroids/ |title=Electric hoedown with hillbillies on steroids |last=Sanford |first=Jay Allen |date=August 1, 2019 |publisher=San Diego Reader |access-date=2022-04-22}}</ref> and [[Gretchen Wilson]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://gazettereview.com/gretchen-wilson-doing-now-update/ |title=What Happened To Gretchen Wilson \u2013 What's She Doing Now in 2022 |last=Rogers |first=Bridget |date=March 28, 2022 |publisher=Gazette Review |access-date=2022-04-22}}</ref>\n\nOn April 10, 2006, [[Country Music Television|CMT]] honored Williams with the [[Johnny Cash]] Visionary Award, presenting it to him at the 2006 [[CMT Music Awards]]. On November 11, 2008, Williams was honored as a [[Broadcast Music Incorporated|BMI]] Icon at the 56th annual BMI Country Awards. The artists and songwriters named BMI Icons have had \"a unique and indelible influence on generations of music makers\".<ref>{{cite web|url= http://www.bmi.com/news/entry/537255 |title=Hank Williams, Jr. to be Honored as Icon at 56th Annual BMI Country Awards|website=Bmi.com|access-date=October 5, 2010|date=September 17, 2008}}</ref>\n\nIn 2015, Williams was inducted into the Louisiana Music Hall of Fame. On August 12, 2020, Williams was selected to be inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum|Country Music Hall of Fame]].<ref name=\"Paulson\"/>\n\n==Personal life==\nHis daughter Katherine Williams-Dunning, the only one of his five children to not pursue a music career, died in a car crash on June 13, 2020, at age 27.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/hank-williams-jr-daughter-katherine-williams-dunning-killed-in-car-accident-tennessee/|title=Daughter of country music legend Hank Williams Jr. dies in car crash, authorities say|website=Cbsnews.com|date=June 14, 2020 |access-date=November 5, 2020}}</ref> His son Shelton performs as [[Hank Williams III]]; his other children include [[Holly Williams (musician)|Holly Williams]]<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.al.com/life/2021/06/hank-jrs-son-following-in-footsteps-of-legendary-grandpa-hank-williams.html |title=Hank Jr.'s son following in footsteps of legendary grandpa Hank Williams? |last=Colurso |first=Mary |website=al.com |date=June 8, 2021 |access-date=July 23, 2021 }}</ref> who is also a musician, as is his grandson [[Coleman Williams]] (Hank III's son), who performs under the sobriquet \"IV\".<ref name=hank3sonIV>{{cite web |last1=Trigger |title=The Hank Williams Lineage Continues with Hank3's Son \"IV\" |url=https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/the-hank-williams-linage-continues-with-hank3s-son-iv/ |website=Saving Country Music|date=March 7, 2021 }}</ref>  His wife Mary Jane Thomas died on March 22, 2022, aged 58, after complications from a medical procedure.<ref>{{Cite web |last1=Avila |first1=Daniela |date=March 23, 2022 |first2=Sarah |last2=Michaud |title=Hank Williams Jr.'s Wife Mary Jane Thomas Has Died: 'A Beautiful Soul' |url=https://people.com/country/hank-williams-jr-wife-mary-jane-dead/ |access-date=2022-03-24 |website=PEOPLE.com |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Hank Williams Jr.'s Wife Mary Jane Thomas Dead at 58 |url=https://www.tmz.com/2022/03/23/hank-williams-jr-wife-dead-dies-mary-jane-thomas/ |access-date=2022-03-24 |website=TMZ|date=March 23, 2022 }}</ref> On September 9, 2023, Williams married his long-time friend since 2003, Brandi. The couple became engaged on Mother's Day of that same year.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Denis |first=Kyle |date=September 12, 2023 |title=Hank Williams Jr. Gets Married in Alabama |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/hank-williams-jr-wedding-married-brandi-1235411287/ |access-date=September 19, 2024 |work=Billboard}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |last=Wilson |first=Angela |date=September 12, 2023 |title=Hank Williams Jr. Marries Fianc\u00e9e Brandi in Alabama Days After Announcing Engagement |url=https://people.com/hank-williams-jr-marries-brandi-in-front-of-a-small-group-of-family-and-friends-in-alabama-7968399 |access-date=September 19, 2024 |work=People}}</ref>\n\n==Politics==\nWilliams has been politically involved with the [[Republican Party (United States)|Republican Party]]. For the [[2000 U.S. Presidential election|2000 U.S. presidential election]], he rerecorded his song \"We Are Young Country\" to \"This is Bush-Cheney Country\". On October 15, 2008, at a rally in [[Virginia Beach, Virginia|Virginia Beach]] for Republican presidential nominee [[John McCain]], he performed \"McCain-Palin Tradition\", a song in support of McCain and his running mate, [[Sarah Palin]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://marcambinder.theatlantic.com/archives/2008/10/the_mccainpalin_tradition.php|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090206023625/http://marcambinder.theatlantic.com/archives/2008/10/the_mccainpalin_tradition.php|url-status=dead|title=\"McCain\u2013Palin Tradition\"|archive-date=February 6, 2009|access-date=November 5, 2020}}</ref> He has contributed to federal election campaigns, mostly to Republicans, including [[Michele Bachmann]]'s 2012 presidential campaign. However, he has donated to some Democrats in the past, most notably [[Jim Cooper]] and [[John S. Tanner]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.newsmeat.com/celebrity_political_donations/Hank_Williams_Jr.php|title=Hank Williams Jr.|publisher=Federal Campaign Contribution Report|access-date=November 27, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130921054027/http://www.newsmeat.com/celebrity_political_donations/Hank_Williams_Jr.php|archive-date=September 21, 2013|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn November 2008, Williams considered a run for the 2012 Republican nomination as a [[U.S. Senator]] from Tennessee for the seat held by GOP incumbent [[Bob Corker]], although his publicist said regarding Williams \"no announcement has been made\".<ref>{{cite news|url=http://realclearpolitics.blogs.time.com/2008/11/25/hank-williams-jr-for-senate |title=Hank Williams Jr. For Senate? - Real Clear Politics \u2013 TIME.com |publisher=Realclearpolitics.blogs.time.com |date=November 25, 2008 |access-date=November 27, 2011 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120128170506/http://realclearpolitics.blogs.time.com/2008/11/25/hank-williams-jr-for-senate/|archive-date=January 28, 2012 }}</ref> Williams ultimately did not run.\n\n===2011 ''Fox and Friends'' controversy===\nIn an October 3, 2011, interview with [[Fox News Channel]]'s ''[[Fox & Friends]]'', Williams discussed a June golf game where President [[Barack Obama]] and Republican House Speaker [[John Boehner]] had teamed against Vice President [[Joe Biden]] and Ohio Governor [[John Kasich]], saying the match was \"one of the biggest political mistakes ever\". When asked why the golf game troubled him, Williams stated, \"Come on. That'd be like Hitler playing golf with [[Benjamin Netanyahu|Netanyahu]]&nbsp;... in the shape this country is in?\" He also said that the President and Vice President were \"the enemy\" and compared them to \"the [[Three Stooges]]\". Later, anchor [[Gretchen Carlson]] said to him, \"You used the name of one of the most hated people in all of the world to describe, ''I think'', the president.\" Williams replied, \"Well, that is true. But I'm telling you like it is.\" As a result of his statements, [[ESPN]] dropped Williams' opening song from its ''[[Monday Night Football]]'' broadcast of the [[Tampa Bay Buccaneers]] versus the [[Indianapolis Colts]] and replaced it with the [[The Star-Spangled Banner|national anthem]].{{citation needed|date=June 2020}}\n\nWilliams later said his analogy was \"extreme \u2013 but it was to make a point\", and \"some of us have strong opinions and are often misunderstood&nbsp;... I was simply trying to explain how stupid it seemed to me \u2013 how ludicrous that pairing was. They're polar opposites, and it made no sense. They don't see eye to eye and never will\". Additionally, Williams said he has \"always respected the office of the president ... Working-class people are hurting \u2013 and it doesn't seem like anybody cares. When both sides are high-fiving it on the ninth hole when everybody else is without a job \u2013 it makes a whole lot of us angry. Something has to change. The policies have to change\". ESPN later said it was \"extremely disappointed\" in Williams' comments, and pulled his opening from that night's broadcast.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://sportsillustrated.cnn.com/2011/football/nfl/10/03/espn.williams.ap/index.html |title=ESPN pulls Hank Williams Jr. intro after singer links Obama with Hitler |publisher=Sportsillustrated.cnn.com |date=October 3, 2011 |access-date=November 27, 2011 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111113134647/http://sportsillustrated.cnn.com/2011/football/nfl/10/03/espn.williams.ap/index.html |archive-date=November 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\nThree days later, ESPN announced Williams and his song would not return to ''Monday Night Football'', ending the use of the song that had been part of the broadcast on both ABC and ESPN since 1989.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.espn.com/nfl/story/_/id/7066449/espn-hank-williams-jr-theme-song-return-monday-night-football|title=ESPN, Hank Williams Jr. part ways|date=October 6, 2010|work=ESPN.com}}</ref> Williams expressed defiance and indifference on his website, and said he was the one who had made the decision. \"After reading hundreds of e-mails, I have made MY decision,\" he wrote. \"By pulling my opening Oct 3rd, You (ESPN) stepped on the Toes of The First Amendment Freedom of Speech, so therefore Me, My Song, and All My Rowdy Friends are OUT OF HERE. It's been a great run.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.espn.com/nfl/story/_/id/7066449/espn-hank-williams-jr-theme-song-return-monday-night-football |title=ESPN \u2013 Hank Williams Jr. theme song won't return to Monday Night Football \u2013 ESPN |publisher=ESPN |date=October 6, 2011 |access-date=November 27, 2011}}</ref> Williams' son, [[Hank Williams III]], stayed neutral in the debate, telling [[TMZ.com]] that most musicians, including his father, are \"not worthy\" of a political discussion.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tmz.com/2011/10/04/hank-williams-jr-monday-night-football-son-politics-obama-hitler-fox-news-channel-jello-biafra-green-party-politics/ |title=Hank Williams Jr.'s Son \u2013 My Dad Should NOT Talk Politics |publisher=TMZ.com |date=November 22, 2011 |access-date=November 27, 2011}}</ref>\n\nAfter his song was pulled from ''Monday Night Football,'' Williams recorded a song criticizing Obama, ESPN and ''[[Fox & Friends]]'', titled \"[[Keep the Change (Hank Williams Jr. song)|Keep the Change]]\". He released the track on [[iTunes]] and via free download at his website.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://content.usatoday.com/communities/gameon/post/2011/10/hank-williams-jr-retaliates-with-song-that-slams-fox/1|title=Hank Williams Jr. retaliates with song that slams Fox|first=Tom|last=Weir|date=October 10, 2011|work=[[USA Today]]}}</ref> The song garnered over 180,000 downloads in two days.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1672429/hank-williams-jr-thrives-with-downloads-media-coverage-surrounding-controversy.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111014104416/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1672429/hank-williams-jr-thrives-with-downloads-media-coverage-surrounding-controversy.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=October 14, 2011|title=Hank Williams Jr. Thrives With Downloads, Media Coverage Surrounding Controversy|date=October 12, 2011|publisher=[[CMT News]]}}</ref>\n\nWilliams continued to make his opinions of Obama known and during a performance at the Iowa State Fair in August 2012, [[Barack Obama religion conspiracy theories|he called Obama a Muslim]] telling the crowd, \"We've got a Muslim president who hates farming, hates the military, hates the U.S. and we hate him!\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/OTUS/hank-williams-jr-tells-crowd-obama-muslim-hates/story?id=17042110|title=Country Star Calls Obama 'a Muslim'|date=August 20, 2012|publisher=ABC News}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Couch |first=Aaron |url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/general-news/hank-williams-jr-songs-barack-obama-363946/ |title=Hank Williams Jr. Calls Obama 'Muslim' Who 'Hates The Military'|work=[[Hollywood Reporter]] |date=August 18, 2012 |access-date=July 5, 2023 |archive-date=July 5, 2023 |archive-url=https://archive.today/20230705214720/https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/general-news/hank-williams-jr-songs-barack-obama-363946/}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|Hank Williams Jr. He is the bassist for [[Shooter Jennings]]' backing band. As a solo artist, Kamp has released 11 albums.\n\n==Biography==\nBorn in New York, Kamp grew up in the Northeast U.S. before moving to Seattle where he began his music career. He fronted a trio, Ponticello, which released four albums. During this time, Kamp released his first solo album, ''Dedications'' (1996). Kamp moved to Los Angeles in 2001 and started a new group, Union Pacific. He performed with other bands and worked as a session musician before being hired as the bassist for Shooter Jennings' band, the .357s.<ref>{{cite web|last=Ruhlmann|first=William|title=Artist Biography |url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/ted-russell-kamp-mn0000053934/biography|website=[[Allmusic]]|accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref>\n\nKamp also continued his solo career, with his album Divisadero<ref>{{cite web|title=Album Review: Ted Russell Kamp - Divisadero|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/divisadero-mw0000565354 |website=Allmusic|accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref><ref>\n{{cite journal | date=March\u2013April 2007| title=Album Review: Ted Russell Kamp - Divisadero | last = Berick | first = Michael | journal=[[No Depression (magazine)|No Depression]]| volume=1| issue=68 | url=http://nodepression.com/album-review/ted-russell-kamp-divisadero| issn=1088-4971| accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref> ranked as #34 on the [[Americana Music Association]]'s 2007 chart.\n\nIn 2011, Kamp released Get Back to the Land,<ref>{{cite web|title=Album Review: Ted Russell Kamp - Get Back to the Land|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/get-back-to-the-land-mw0002092965 |website=Allmusic|accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref> which made the top 25 on the Americana Radio Chart and was #1 on the Euro Americana Chart.\n\nIn January 2013, Kamp released Night Owl,<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Music: Ted Russell Kamp - Night Owl|url=http://www.popmatters.com/review/170077-ted-russell-kamp-night-owl/ |magazine=[[PopMatters]]|accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref> which made the US Americana Radio Chart (#34) and the Euro Americana Chart (#15).\n\nKamp self-released ''The Low and Lonesome Sound'' in 2015, followed a year later by the acoustic album ''Flying Solo''.<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Music: Ted Russell Kamp - The Low and Lonesome Sound|url=http://www.popmatters.com/review/ted-russell-kamp-the-low-and-lonesome-sound/ |magazine=PopMatters|accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Bassist Ted Russell Kamp, Flying Solo...|date=8 April 2016 |url=http://bassmusicianmagazine.com/2016/04/flying-solo-featuring-bassist-ted-russell-kamp/ |publisher=[[Bass Musician]]|accessdate=May 30, 2017}}</ref> He joined Ted Wulfers to record the classic song Tulsa Time to help support the Red Cross of Oklahoma. 100% of the proceeds were donated to The Oklahoma Red Cross.\n\nKamp is also an established producer in the music industry.\n\n==Discography==\n===Solo albums===\n* 1996: ''Dedications'' (Poetry Of The Moment [PoMo])\n* 2005: ''Northsouth'' (PoMo)\n* 2005: ''The Ponticello Years'' (Kufala)\n* 2006: ''Nashville Fineline'' (Kufala)\n* 2007: ''Divisadero'' (PoMo)\n* 2008: ''Poor Man's Paradise'' ([[Dualtone Records|Dualtone]] / PoMo)\n* 2010: ''California Country Soul, Vol. 2 : Ballads'' (PoMo)\n* 2011: ''Get Back To The Land'' ([[Dualtone Records|Dualtone]] / PoMo)\n* 2013: ''Night Owl'' (PoMo)\n* 2015: ''The Low and Lonesome Sound'' (self-released via [[CD Baby]])\n* 2016: ''Flying Solo'' [Audio & Video Labs, Inc.)\n* 2019: ''Walkin' Shoes'' (PoMo Records)\n\n===With [[Shooter Jennings]]===\n* 2005: ''[[Put the \"O\" Back in Country]]'' ([[Show Dog-Universal Music|Universal South]])\n* 2006: ''[[Electric Rodeo (Shooter Jennings album)|Electric Rodeo]]'' ([[Show Dog-Universal Music|Universal South]])\n* 2006: ''[[Live at Irving Plaza 4.18.06]]'' ([[Show Dog-Universal Music|Universal South]])\n* 2014: ''Don't Wait Up (For George)'' EP ([[Black Country Rock Media|Black Country Rock]])\n* 2016: ''[[Black Ribbons]]'' ([[Black Country Rock Media|Black Country Rock]])\n* 2016: ''[[Countach (For Giorgio)]]'' ([[Black Country Rock Media|Black Country Rock]])\n\n===As primary artist/song contributor===\n* 2009: various artists - This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Flatlanders","to":"The Flatlanders"}],"pages":{"1980798":{"pageid":1980798,"ns":0,"title":"The Flatlanders","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use American English|date=July 2023}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=July 2023}}\n{{Short description|American country band}}\n{{Refimprove|date=July 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n|name            = The Flatlanders\n|image           = Flatlanders.gif\n|caption         = The Flatlanders playing a concert in [[Lubbock, Texas]], on June 3, 2009\n|image_size      = \n|background      = group_or_band\n|origin          = [[Lubbock, Texas]], U.S.\n|genre           = [[Country rock]], [[alternative country]]\n|years_active    = 1972\u20131973, 1998\u2013present\n|label           = Charly, [[New West Records|New West]], [[Plantation Records|Plantation]], [[Rounder Records|Rounder]]\n|associated_acts = \n|website         =  \n|current_members = [[Jimmie Dale Gilmore]]<br /> [[Joe Ely]]<br /> [[Butch Hancock]]\n}}\n\n'''The Flatlanders''' are an American [[country music|country band]] from [[Lubbock, Texas]], founded in 1972 by [[Jimmie Dale Gilmore]], [[Joe Ely]] and [[Butch Hancock]].<ref>{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p1606/biography}}</ref> The group garnered little success during their brief original incarnation from 1972 to 1973, but when the individual members found success in their solo careers, interest in The Flatlanders was rekindled with the band reuniting several times since. An earlier incarnation of this band was known as The Double Mountain Fork Of The Brazos River Boys.\n\n==History==\nIn 1972, Gilmore, Ely and Hancock, formed The Flatlanders with each contributing vocals, guitar, and songwriting skills. Other key musicians were Steve Wesson on [[autoharp]] and [[musical saw]], Tony Pearson on [[mandolin]] and backup harmony, [[Tommy Hancock]] (no relation to Butch Hancock) on [[fiddle]] and Syl Rice on [[string bass]].\n\nOne of the band's first appearances was at the [[Kerrville Folk Festival]] in 1972, where they were named one of the winners of the inaugural Kerrville Folk Festival New Folk Singer/Songwriter Competition.\n\nThe band's first recording project was produced in 1972 by Shelby Singleton, the then-owner of [[Memphis, Tennessee|Memphis, Tennessee's]] famed [[Sun Studios]]. A promotional single, Gilmore's \"Dallas\", was a commercial failure, and the planned album, ''All American Music'', was all but scrapped, being released only in a limited run on [[Stereo 8|8-track tape]] in order to fulfill contractual obligations. \n\nThe Flatlanders performed through 1973 before disbanding. By the end of the decade, however, Gilmore, Ely and Hancock had all found success as solo performers, and rumors of their earlier obscure collaboration began to circulate. In 1990, [[Rounder Records]] issued the 1972 sessions as ''More a Legend Than a Band''.\n\nThe three musicians continued to reunite for occasional Flatlanders performances. In 1998 they contributed to the soundtrack of ''[[The Horse Whisperer (film)|The Horse Whisperer]]'', and then in 2002 released their follow-up album, ''Now Again,'' on [[New West Records]].  In 2004 this was followed with ''Wheels of Fortune'', again on New West. In 2004, New West released ''Live '72'' a live recording of the then-unknown country band performing at the One Knite [[honky-tonk]] in [[Austin, Texas]].\n\nIn 2009, The Flatlanders released the album, ''Hills & Valleys''. In promotion of the album, the group appeared as musical guests on the ''Late Show with David Letterman'' on July 21, 2009, and on Garrison Keillor's ''A Prairie Home Companion'' on April 27, 2013.\n\nIn 2012, The Flatlanders released ''The Odessa Tapes'', an album composed of unreleased recordings culled from 1972 recording sessions.<ref>{{cite web |title=Song Premiere: The Flatlanders, 'Shadow Of The Moon' |date=June 11, 2012 |url=http://www.americansongwriter.com/2012/06/song-premiere-the-flatlanders-shadow-of-the-moon/ |publisher=America Songwriter |accessdate=June 14, 2012}}</ref>\n\nThe Flatlanders were voted into the Austin Music Awards Hall of Fame in March 2016. <ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.dailytexanonline.com/2016/03/16/country-band-the-flatlanders-inducted-into-austin-music-awards-hall-of-fame|title=Country band The Flatlanders inducted into Austin Music Awards Hall of Fame - The Daily Texan|website=Dailytexanonline.com}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n!rowspan=\"2\" \"'''Shooter'''\" '''Jennings''' (born May 19, 1979) is an American musician and record producer. He is the son of [[Country music|country]] singers [[Waylon Jennings]] and [[Jessi Colter]]. In a career spanning three decades, Jennings has explored a variety of musical genres.\n\nJennings made his debut with the single \"4th of July\" of his 2005 album ''[[Put the \"O\" Back in Country]]'' on [[Universal South Records|Universal South]], which peaked at No. 22 on the Billboard country charts.<ref>{{Cite web|title = Shooter Jennings - Chart history {{!}} Billboard|url = http://www.billboard.com/artist/279176/shooter-jennings/chart?f=320|website = www.billboard.com|access-date = November 21, 2015}}</ref> Jennings has since followed with seven full-length studio albums: ''[[Electric Rodeo (Shooter Jennings album)|Electric Rodeo]]'' (2006), ''[[The Wolf (Shooter Jennings album)|The Wolf]]'' (2007), ''[[Black Ribbons]]'' (2009), ''Family Man'' (2012), ''The Other Life'' (2013) ''[[Countach (For Giorgio)]]'' (2016), and ''Shooter'' (2018), in addition to a live album, a compilation, and numerous [[Extended play|EPs]].\n\n== Early life ==\nJennings was born in [[Nashville, Tennessee]], on May 19, 1979. There are two different accounts regarding how he got his nickname \"Shooter.\" His mother cited her, and husband Waylon Jennings', love of western culture and cowboy art for inspiring the gun-derived moniker. But his father said he came up with the name when, moments after the newborn emerged from his mother's womb, the boy sprayed a nurse before anyone could put on his first diaper. \"I love my mom,\" says Jennings, \"but I like Dad's version better. And I believe it's true. He didn't make [stuff] like that up.\"\n\nHe lived the first few years of his life in a crib on his parents' tour bus surrounded by the likes of [[Johnny Cash]], [[Willie Nelson]] and [[Kris Kristofferson]]. By age 5, he was playing drums. At 8 years old, he began taking piano lessons. He started playing guitar at 14 and on occasion he'd play percussion in his father's band.\n\nIn high school Jennings fronted an industrial rock band called KilRaven for his high school's talent show. In 2011, he released the KilRaven track \"Only You\" on the album \"Missed The Boat\".\n\nIn 1996, Jennings and his father recorded an album together. They called it ''Fenixon'' (a play on the words \"phoenix\" and \"son\") but could not find a label to distribute it.<ref>{{Cite news|title = Waylon and Son, Reunited on Disc|url = https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB122471459623460261|newspaper = Wall Street Journal|access-date = November 21, 2015|issn = 0099-9660|first = Jim|last = Fusilli}}</ref> Some of the material was remastered and used for the album ''Waylon Forever''. The full ''Fenixon'' recording was finally released by Jennings' label Black Country Rock in 2014. Shooter Jennings is the uncle of William Harness, Professionally known as [[Struggle Jennings]].\n\n== Career ==\n[[File:Shooterjennings(by Scott Dudelson).jpg|thumb|Jennings performing in 2009]]\n\n=== Stargunn ===\nIn 2001, Jennings left [[Nashville, Tennessee]], to seek his fortunes in [[Los Angeles]]. He assembled and performed with Stargunn, a [[rock music|rock]] band. The band featured Jennings on piano and lead vocals, Carter Falco, and Jonathan Boddie (later succeeded by Kevin Sciou) on guitar and background vocals, Curtis Roach on bass, and Lex Lipsitz on drums. Towards the end of 2001, Stargunn released their first album, ''The Only Way Up Is Down'', and toured with [[Saliva (band)|Saliva]], [[Tesla (band)|Tesla]], Mark Ford and others in support of the album. That same year, ''[[Music Connection]]'' magazine listed Stargunn as one of the Hot 100 Unsigned Artists of 2001.\n\nIn 2002, Stargunn was featured on ''I've Always Been Crazy: A Tribute to Waylon Jennings'', and the soundtrack to the [[Vince Vaughn]] film ''[[Made (2001 film)|Made]]''. Shortly after, [[Touchstone Pictures]] licensed the song \"White Lines N Black Ties\" for the film ''[[The Crew (2000 film)|The Crew]]'' starring [[Burt Reynolds]]. Stargunn performed together for three years, built an avid following, and earned praise from the local music press. On March 30, 2003, Jennings dissolved Stargunn and began working on his solo career.\n\nAfter the band's breakup, Jennings was twice presented with the opportunity to front the hard rock supergroup [[Velvet Revolver]], but chose instead to pursue a solo career.<ref>{{Cite web|title = SHOOTER JENNINGS Claims He Was Offered VELVET REVOLVER Job Twice|url = http://www.blabbermouth.net/news/shooter-jennings-claims-he-was-offered-velvet-revolver-job-twice/|website = BLABBERMOUTH.NET|date = March 19, 2009|access-date = November 21, 2015|language = en-US}}</ref>\n\nIn 2015, Jennings' label Black Country Rock released Stargunn's debut album \"The Only Way Up Is Down\" on vinyl as part of Record Store Day.\n\n=== ''Put the \"O\" Back in Country'' ===\nHe returned to Los Angeles in 2004 to begin working on new material. In 2005 Jennings signed his first recording contract, with [[Universal South Records]], releasing his debut album ''[[Put the \"O\" Back in Country]]'' that same year.\n\n\"Put the \"O\" Back in Country\" produced his only entry on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts in its lead-off single \"Fourth of July\", which peaked at No.&nbsp;22. The album version of this song features a cameo appearance by George Jones, who sings the chorus to his signature song \"He Stopped Loving Her Today\" at the end; this guest appearance was removed from the song's radio edit. Despite the edit, Jones was credited on the Billboard charts. The album featured his new band The .357's, which consisted of Leroy Powell on guitar, Bryan Keeling on drums, [[Ted Russell Kamp|Ted Kamp]] on bass with [[Robby Turner]] on steel, and backing vocals by [[Bonnie Bramlett]].\n\nLater that year his song \"Busted In Baylor County\" was then featured in the 2005 film version of ''[[The Dukes of Hazzard (film)|The Dukes of Hazzard]]'', furthermore Jennings portrayed his father in the [[Johnny Cash]] [[Biographical film|biopic]] ''[[Walk the Line]]'' alongside [[Joaquin Phoenix]] and [[Reese Witherspoon]]. His rendition of his father's song \"Long Way From Home\" was featured on the film's soundtrack.\n\n=== ''Electric Rodeo'' and ''The Wolf'' ===\nThough recorded before ''Put the \"O\" Back in Country'', released on April 4, 2006,{{clarify|reason=is this the release date of Put the O Back in Country or the release date of Electric Rodeo?|date=April 2017}} ''[[Electric Rodeo (Shooter Jennings album)|Electric Rodeo]]'' was released as Jennings's second solo album. Sonically, ''Electric Rodeo'' is louder, rawer, more upfront rock and roll than its predecessor.\n\n''Electric Rodeo'' was followed by ''[[The Wolf (Shooter Jennings album)|The Wolf]]'' on October 23, 2007. The album varied from his previous records in that the .357s had opted for a decidedly 1970s feel to the instrumentals. It featured collaborations with [[Doug Kershaw]] and [[The Oak Ridge Boys]], as well as a cover of the [[Dire Straits]] song \"[[Walk of Life]]\".\n\nThat same year Jennings was featured on a duet of \"[[Good Hearted Woman (song)|Good Hearted Woman]]\" on [[Deana Carter]]'s sixth studio album, ''[[The Chain (Deana Carter album)|The Chain]]''.\n\n=== Departure from Universal ===\nIn 2009, Jennings, having issues with his label and wanting out of his four-album contract released his first compilation album, ''[[Bad Magick: The Best of Shooter Jennings and the .357's]]''. The album featured four new tracks; live versions of \"Lonesome Blues\", and \"Daddy's Farm\", as well as covers of his father's \"Lonesome, Onry and Mean\", and the [[Hank Williams, Jr.]] song \"Living Proof\".\n\nAfter the release of ''Bad Magick: The Best of Shooter Jennings and the .357's'', having fulfilled his four-album contract; Jennings parted ways with Universal records.\n\nOn March 23, 2009, Jennings took part in ''[[CMT Crossroads]]'', a television show in which two musicians are paired with one another and perform a small concert together for an intimate crowd. The episode paired Jennings with close friend and fellow musician [[Jamey Johnson]]. The evening's set list consisted entirely of duets, including a cover of \"[[Outlaw country|Outlaw]] Shit\" from the ''[[Waylon Forever]]'' album, two songs from Jennings' discography; \"God Bless Alabama\", \"It Ain't Easy\". As well as four songs from Johnson's album ''[[That Lonesome Song]]''; \"High Cost Of Living\", \"Mowing Down The Roses\", \"Between Jennings and Jones\" and \"In Color\".\n\n=== ''Black Ribbons'' ===\nHaving left Universal, Jennings changed the name of his backing band from The .357's to Hierophant. With the news that he and his band would be joining the likes of [[Paramore]], [[Bad Religion]], [[Fall Out Boy]], [[Jefree Star]], and various other popular rock bands on the 2009 [[Warped Tour]] it became apparent that Jennings next album would differ drastically from his previous efforts.\n\nIn February 2009, it was announced that the album would be titled ''[[Black Ribbons]]''. It was also announced that it would be a dystopian concept rock opera and that writer [[Stephen King]] would play a major role in the album as Will O' The Wisp.\n\nIt was released independently on March 2, 2010, through Black Country Rock Records, and although it was seen as a complete departure from his country sound, the album showed off the diversity as an artist and gained him much critical acclaim, as well as a brand new underground following.\n\nOn May 1, 2010, Jennings announced \"Black Ribbons: The Living Album\" on his Twitter account.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/ShooterJennings |title=Shooter Jennings (ShooterJennings) on Twitter |publisher=Twitter.com |date=June 3, 2014 |access-date=August 4, 2014}}</ref> The \"Living Album\" includes the full studio record and live shows with [[Hierophant]] on a [[USB flash drive]] shaped like a tarot card.\nTowards the end of 2010, Jennings with the help of various other artists launched the \"XXX\" movement to help musicians who struggle to receive mainstream recognition.\n\nIn 2016, Jennings created and released a podcast series title \"Beyond the Black\" dealing with the topics and recording of [[Black Ribbons]]. The series is available on all music streaming formats as well as YouTube and the podcast's own website: [http://www.beyondthe.black www.beyondthe.black]\n\n=== ''Family Man'' ===\nIn 2011, along with childhood friend and master pianist Erik Deutsch, Jennings formed The Triple Crown, a new backing band featuring Erik Deutsch on piano, Tony Leone on drums, Jeff Hill on bass, Jon Graboff on pedal steel, Eleanor Whitmore on fiddle and Chris Masterson on lead guitar.\n\nOn March 13, 2012, having signed a record deal with [[E1 Music]], and with The Triple Crown along for the ride, Jennings returned to his country roots with the release of the album ''Family Man'', his first self-produced outing. The album was originally meant to contain eighteen tracks, but was instead split into two albums: ''Family Man'' and 2013's ''The Other Life''.\n\nOn July 31, 2012, Jennings was featured in [[Bucky Covington]]'s debut single \"The Drinking Side of Country\" from the album ''Good Guys''.\n\nJennings took part in the February 25 Johnny Cash 80th Birthday Bash, in which he sang [[Cocaine Blues]] With [[Willie Nelson]] and [[Amy Nelson]]. The performance was released in a DVD/CD combo.\n\nIn October 2012 Jennings was one of six commentators for the Ovation mini-series ''Song By Song: Johnny Cash''.\n\n=== ''The Other Life'' ===\nWhile recording ''Family Man'', Jennings decided to cut the darker tracks from the album, and instead use them for the album's follow-up, ''The Other Life''.\n\n\"Five of these songs were recorded when we were doing ''Family Man'', and when we were deciding what to do with it we broke it up into two records. ''The Other Life'' is representative of the other side of the coin from ''Family Man'' and the way my life has been going in a lot of ways, At first we were going to call it ''The Outsider'', but once we got into the film we thought, 'Well, it's like a mirror, a dark mirror of what ''Family Man'' was.{{'\"}} - Jennings told TheBoot.com.\n\nJennings premiered the track \"Wild & Lonesome\" (featuring [[Patti Griffin]]) on the 4th season of the FX original series ''[[Sons of Anarchy]]''. Followed by the release of first official single from the album \"The White Trash Song\" (featuring [[Scott H. Biram]]) which premiered on RollingStones.com along with the announcement that the album would be accompanied by a film.\n\nThe album featured seven new songs, as well as two cover songs ([[Harry Nilsson]]'s \"Flying Saucer song\" and [[Steve Young (musician)|Steve Young]]'s \"The White Trash song\") and \"Outlaw You\", which was put out in early 2012 as a digital release.\n\nJennings along with filmmaker Blake Judd released ''The Other Life'' film. Running at 32 minutes long, it utilizes six of the songs from the album as a sort of narration. The film is about a musician leaving his family to tour, but when he does so he finds the road is not the same, and becomes haunted by a mysterious woman. Throughout the film, the musician is forced to face his darker urges and deal with self-discovery, temptation, isolation and rebirth. The film closes with a short adaptation of [[Stephen King]]'s ''[[The Dark Tower (series)|The Dark Tower]]''.\n\nThe Other Life went on to win Best Short Film at the 2013 Horror Hound Festival.\n\nThe album was also heavily featured in the 2nd season of ''[[The Punisher (TV series)|The Punisher]]'', of which Shooter also appears, as himself.\n\n=== Black Country Rock Media ===\n{{main|Black Country Rock Media}}\nIn October 2013, Jennings announced the formation of his new label and multi-format recording company, Black Country Rock. Their initial releases included: a remastered release of the [[Waylon Jennings]] album ''[[Right for the Time]]'', two live albums (one from [[Jessi Colter]] titled ''Live from Cain's Ballroom'', and one from Jennings titled ''The Other Live''), as well as a recording of \"[[You Are My Sunshine]]\" featuring vocals from both [[Jamey Johnson]] and Jennings. All four were released on vinyl, cassette, CD, as well as digitally.\n\n=== ''The Magic'' ===\nOn February 27, 2014, Jennings revealed he would be releasing a spoken word follow-up to Hierophant's 2010 album, ''[[Black Ribbons]]'', titled ''The Magic'', inspired by first story in the controversially interactive horror series thirteen.\n\nIn addition to ''The Magic'' Jennings also announced, that after nearly a decade of waiting, he would be releasing the 1995 collaborative album, ''Fenixon''.\n\nBoth projects were released during 2014's Record Store Day, and subsequently sold out.\n\n=== \"George/Giorgio\" releases ===\nTowards the end of May 2014, Jennings announced his intention to release two EP's later in the year. ''Don't Wait Up (for George)'' is a tribute to his close friend and mentor [[George Jones]], which was released in August 2014. Jennings' seventh studio album, ''[[Countach (For Giorgio)]]'', was originally scheduled to be released in November 2014, but its release was delayed due to the sudden death of [[Jon Hensley (radio personality)|Jon Hensley]], Jennings' longtime manager and friend and Black Country Rock co-founder.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.laweekly.com/music/how-daft-punk-and-the-muppets-inspired-shooter-jennings-giorgio-moroder-tribute-album-6616503 |title=How Daft Punk and the Muppets Inspired Shooter Jennings' Giorgio Moroder Tribute Album |first=Daniel |last=Kohn |work=[[LA Weekly]] |publisher=[[Voice Media Group]] |date=February 23, 2016 |access-date=March 2, 2016}}</ref> A tribute to 1970s electronic-music pioneer and producer, [[Giorgio Moroder]], the album was released on February 26, 2016, and features guest vocals from [[Steve Young (musician)|Steve Young]],<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/6882805/shooter-jennings-giorgio-moroder-tribute-album-countach-david-bowie-interview |title=Shooter Jennings on Giorgio Moroder Tribute Album & How His David Bowie Cover 'Ended Up Meaning So Much More' |first=Chuck |last=Dauphin |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |publisher=[[Prometheus Global Media]] |date=February 19, 2016 |access-date=March 2, 2016}}</ref> [[Brandi Carlile]],<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/shooter-jennings-enlists-marilyn-manson-brandi-carlile-for-countach-20160104 |title=Shooter Jennings Enlists Marilyn Manson, Brandi Carlile for 'Countach' |first=Andrew |last=Leahey |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=January 4, 2016 |access-date=March 2, 2016}}</ref> [[Marilyn Manson]]<ref>{{cite web |url=http://consequenceofsound.net/2016/02/marilyn-manson-covers-the-hell-out-of-david-bowies-cat-people-listen/ |title=Marilyn Manson covers the hell out of David Bowie's \"Cat People\" \u2014 listen |first=Ben |last=Kaye |work=[[Consequence of Sound]] |date=February 18, 2016 |access-date=March 2, 2016}}</ref> and [[Richard Garriott|Richard Garriott de Cayeux]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.avclub.com/article/neon-noir-meets-outlaw-country-shooter-jennings-tr-230314 |title=Neon noir meets outlaw country in Shooter Jennings' tribute to Giorgio Moroder |first=Mike |last=Vanderbilt |work=[[The A.V. Club]] |publisher=[[The Onion]] |date=January 5, 2016 |access-date=March 2, 2016}}</ref> The album became his first to enter the Dance Albums chart, peaking at number seven there.<ref name=\"dance\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/shooter-jennHOOings/chart-history/dance-electronic-albums|title=Shooter Jennings - Chart history {{!}} Billboard|website=www.billboard.com|language=en|access-date=March 17, 2017}} {{dead link|date=December 2021|bot=medic}}{{cbignore|bot=medic}}</ref>\n\n=== ''Shooter'' ===\n\nFollowing Countach, [[Brandi Carlile]] insisted that Jennings be involved in her next project. Together with [[Dave Cobb]], Jennings produced her 2018 album ''[[By the Way, I Forgive You]]'', which landed six Grammy nominations, including the all-genre Album and Song of the Year categories. It won in three categories: Americana album and both best American roots song and best American roots performance (for \"The Joke\").\n\nAfter reuniting with Dave Cobb, with whom Jennings made his first four records, Jennings, inspired by the 1984 country album ''[[Major Moves]]'' decided to shelve the album he had already been working on and instead go in a completely different direction with Cobb and make a fun, straight-ahead drinking, rockin' record. That album, titled ''Shooter'', was released in August 2018. \n \nThe following year Jennings teamed up with Brandi Carlile to produce [[Tanya Tucker]]'s 25th album, ''[[While I'm Livin']]''. The record, Tucker's first in 17 years, earned Grammys for Best Country Album and Best Country Song as well as Americana Award nominations for Album of the Year, Song of the Year and Artist of the Year.\n\n=== ''Over a Cocaine Rainbow'' ===\n\nIn late 2021 Jennings released \"Leave Those Memories Alone\", a tribute to his late friend and manager, Col. John Hensley. the track serves as the first single from the album ''Over a Cocaine Rainbow''. The record was initially slated for a 2017 release, but Jennings felt it was too \"dark and experimental\" to release at the time, given its subject matter and tone. Earlier that same year, Jennings released a remix of his \"From Here to Eternity\" track. The new version is dubbed the \"Goof the Floof Remix\", a reference to something Scientology founder [[L. Ron Hubbard]] once said in an interview.\n\n=== Radio show ===\n\nSince 2005, Jennings has hosted \"Shooter Jennings' Electric Rodeo\" on [[Sirius XM]] Outlaw Country channel.<ref>{{cite web|title=SHOOTER JENNINGS DJS ON SIRIUS RADIO|url=http://www.countryweekly.com/news/shooter-jennings-djs-sirius-radio|website=Country Weekly|access-date=November 13, 2015}}</ref> The show's format primarily consists of country, rock, and outlaw music. It airs on Saturday night at 6\u20138&nbsp;pm EST, with a replay on Sunday at 10\u201312&nbsp;pm.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.siriusxm.com/outlawcountry|title=Outlaw Country - Top Country Music with an Edge on SiriusXM|website=Siriusxm.com|access-date=August 11, 2018}}</ref>\n\n=== Production work ===\nJennings collaborated as producer with [[Duff McKagan]] for his 2019 solo album, [[Tenderness (Duff McKagan album)|''Tenderness'']]. The album was recorded with Jennings band, The Waters and The Suicide Horn Section, amongst others.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.blabbermouth.net/news/does-duff-mckagan-feel-underrated-as-a-bass-player/|title=Does DUFF MCKAGAN Feel Underrated As A Bass Player?|date=May 3, 2019|website=BLABBERMOUTH.NET|access-date=August 30, 2019}}</ref> In March 2019, a tour was announced in support of the album, featuring Jennings band playing both the support slot as well as the headline slot as the backing band for Duff.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://ultimateclassicrock.com/duff-mckagan-tenderness-album/|title=Duff McKagan Announces 'Tenderness' Album and Tour Dates|last=Lifton|first=Dave|website=Ultimate Classic Rock|date=March 20, 2019 |language=en|access-date=August 30, 2019}}</ref>\n\nJennings has produced albums and tracks for numerous bands including [[Brandi Carlile]], [[Marilyn Manson]], [[Tanya Tucker]] and [[American Aquarium]], as well as [[Jessi Colter]], [[Jamey Johnson]], [[Jaime Wyatt]], [[The White Buffalo (musician)|The White Buffalo]], [[Hellbound Glory]], [[The Mastersons]], [[Julie Roberts]], [[Yelawolf]], [[Jason Boland & The Stragglers|Jason Boland]], Billy Don Burns, [[Avi Kaplan]], [[Billy Ray Cyrus]], and [[Angry Grandpa]].\n\n== Style and influences ==\nShooter Jennings's influences include [[David Bowie]],<ref name=\"Amorosi\">{{cite web |last=Amorosi |first=A D. |date=August 5, 2016 |title=Shooter Jennings |first=Joseph|date=July 16, 2020 |publisher=Rolling Stone|access-date=January 5, 2023}}</ref> Regarding classification of his music, Jennings said that he did not want to be pigeonholed as being solely a rock musician.<ref name=Dickinson>{{cite web |url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/news/ct-xpm-2006-09-29-0609290188-story.html |title= Shooter Jennings isn't wailin' about forging own identity |url=https://www.revolvermag.com/music/marilyn-manson-southern-new-album-machine-gun-kelly-twins-evil-tour |title=Marilyn Manson on \"Southern\" New Album, Machine Gun Kelly, Twins of Evil Tour described Jennings as having \"established himself as an artist who played by his own rules\" and said that his music is \"strongly informed by both [[hard rock]] and [[outlaw country]]\", while his album ''[[Black Ribbons]]'' \"explored his interest in [[heavy metal music|metal]] and [[electronic music]]\".<ref name=\"allmusic\"/>\n\n== Personal life ==\nJennings is the son of country music singers [[Waylon Jennings]] and [[Jessi Colter]]. He has six half-siblings in total; five from his father, and one, Jennifer Eddy Harness, from his mother. Jennifer's son, country rap artist [[Struggle Jennings]], spent a substantial amount of his adolescence in the company of Shooter (who was one year older than Struggle) and Waylon Jennings.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Struggle Jennings on 'purpose over popularity,' growth in hip-hop-inspired country music |url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/2023/12/13/country-music-artists-struggle-jennings-talks-album-el-camino/71660737007/ |access-date=2024-01-11 |website=The Tennessean |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn February 13, 2002, Shooter's father died in his sleep of diabetic complications in [[Chandler, Arizona]].<ref>{{Cite web|title = Obituaries {{!}} Country singer Waylon Jennings dead at 64 {{!}} Seattle Times Newspaper|url = http://community.seattletimes.nwsource.com/archive/?date=20020213&slug=webjennings13|website = community.seattletimes.nwsource.com|access-date = November 21, 2015}}</ref> He was buried in the Mesa City Cemetery, in [[Mesa, Arizona]].<ref>{{Cite web|title = Waylon wall: Country singer's grave finally has marker - Tucson Citizen Morgue, Part 2 (1993-2009)|url = http://tucsoncitizen.com/morgue2/2003/02/19/134679-waylon-wall-country-singer-s-grave-finally-has-marker/|website = tucsoncitizen.com|access-date = November 21, 2015}}</ref> At the life tribute ceremony, on February 15, Shooter sang \"I've Always Been Crazy\" for the attendees, who included Waylon's close friends, family, and fellow musicians.\n\nJennings began dating actress [[Drea de Matteo]] in 2001.<ref name=\"people2007\">{{cite news |url=http://www.people.com/people/article/0,,20163275,00.html|title=Drea de Matteo Has a Baby Girl|work=People|first=Tim|last=Nudd |date=November 29, 2007|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20080118051339/http://www.people.com/people/article/0,,20163275,00.html|archive-date= January 18, 2008|access-date= February 23, 2022}}</ref> They have two children together, a daughter born in 2007<ref name=\"people2007\"/> and a son born in 2011.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://celebritybabies.people.com/2011/04/08/drea-de-matteo-shooter-jennings-welcome-son-waylon-albert/|archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20180407182731/http://celebritybabies.people.com/2011/04/08/drea-de-matteo-shooter-jennings-welcome-son-waylon-albert/ |archive-date= April 7, 2018|title= Drea de Matteo, Shooter Jennings Welcome Son Waylon Albert|work=People|first=Sarah|last=Michaud|date=April 8, 2011|access-date= February 23, 2022}}</ref> Jennings and de Matteo eventually ended their relationship without marrying.<ref name=\"people2013\">{{cite news |url=http://www.people.com/people/article/0,,20713974,00.html|title=Shooter Jennings & Misty Brooke Swain Marry in the Desert|work=People|first=Cynthia|last=Sanz|date=July 2, 2013|access-date=November 4, 2013}}</ref>\n\nJennings married long-time friend Misty Brooke Swain on June 4, 2013, in [[Joshua Tree, California]].<ref name=\"people2013\"/> Swain and Jennings had met while he was in his rock band, Stargunn, and Swain was bartending at the Rainbow Bar & Grill. Shooter and Misty live in Hollywood, California.\n\n== Discography ==\n{{main|Shooter Jennings discography}}\n;Studio albums\n*''[[Put the \"O\" Back in Country]]'' (2005)\n*''[[Electric Rodeo (Shooter Jennings album)|Electric Rodeo]]'' (2006)\n*''[[The Wolf (Shooter Jennings album)|The Wolf]]'' (2007)\n*''[[Black Ribbons]]'' (2010)\n*''Family Man'' (2012)\t\n*''The Other Life'' (2013)\n*''Fenixon'' <small>(with [[Waylon Jennings]])</small> (2014)\n*''Don't Wait Up (for George) EP'' (2014)\n*''[[Countach (For Giorgio)]]'' (2016)\n*''Shooter'' (2018)\n*''Sometimes Y'' <small>(with [[Yelawolf]])</small> (2022)\n\n== Production discography ==\n'''Studio albums'''\n*''[[Waylon Forever]]'' - This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Black_Tie_(band)","to":"Black Tie (band)"}],"pages":{"23590959":{"pageid":23590959,"ns":0,"title":"Black Tie (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Black Tie\n| image           =\n| caption         =\n| image_size      =\n| alias           =\n| origin          = United States\n| genre           = [[Country rock]]\n| years_active    = 1985-2007\n| label           = Bench, Mastering Pro\n| past_members    = [[Jimmy Griffin]]<br />[[Randy Meisner]]<br />[[Billy Swan]]\n}}\n'''Black Tie''' was an American [[country rock]] [[supergroup (music)|supergroup]] formed by [[Jimmy Griffin]], [[Randy Meisner]], and [[Billy Swan]]. The group's first album, ''When the Night Falls'', was produced by [[Reggie Fisher]] and released on LP in 1985 by Bench Records (BR-001) and reissued on CD in 1990 (BRCD-101). For the CD release the band recorded new versions of two tracks from the LP, \"Learning the Game\", a cover of the [[Buddy Holly]] song, and \"Chain Gang\", a cover of the [[Sam Cooke]] song.<ref>{{cite book|last1=Searles|first1=Malcolm|title=Bread: A Sweet Surrender|date=2014|publisher=Helter Skelter|location=London, England|isbn=978-1-905139-32-3|page=215}}</ref> These tracks were released as a single, and \"Learning the Game\" reached #59 of the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs|Hot Country Singles & Tracks]] chart.\n\nGriffin was formerly a member of the [[soft rock]] band [[Bread (band)|Bread]], and would later chart five country singles as one-third of [[The Remingtons]]. Meisner was formerly a member of [[Poco (band)|Poco]], [[Ricky Nelson]]'s Stone Canyon Band, and the [[Eagles (band)|Eagles]]. Swan had several country hits in the 1970s, including the number one country and pop hit \"[[I Can Help]]\".\n\nWhen Griffin left the group to form the Remingtons, the remaining members, Meisner and Swan, hooked up with Charlie Rich Jr., son and former bandleader for his famous [[Charlie Rich|father]], and began recording in 1992 under the name Meisner, Swan & Rich. Ten tracks were released on an eponymous CD in April 2000 in Japan{{Citation needed|date=April 2023}} (2001 by Varese in the US and 2002 by Rev-Ola in the UK). The same ten songs were reissued in 2006 and 2008 under the title, ''The Eagle, the Dove and the Gold'' on the Sonic Past Music label.\n\nIn 2006, a 3-song EP was released as ''Black Tie Two'' with a version of the classic Christmas carol \"Away in a Manger\", which had been released to country radio as a Christmas single in the late 1980s. It also included the 1992 Meisner, Swan & Rich single \"I'm Sure of You\" and \"Listen to the Radio\".\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n!
