This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Confederate_Railroad","to":"Confederate Railroad"}],"pages":{"3212043":{"pageid":3212043,"ns":0,"title":"Confederate Railroad","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American Southern rock band}}\n{{distinguish|Confederate railroads in the American Civil War}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name             = Confederate Railroad\n| image            = Confederate Railroad2019.jpg\n| image_size       = \n| caption          = Confederate Railroad in 2019.\n| alias            = Confederate RR\n| origin           = [[Atlanta, Georgia]], U.S.\n| genre            = {{flatlist|\n* [[Country rock]]<ref>{{cite web |url=https://ultimateclassicrock.com/confederate-flag-rock-music/ |title=ROCK'S COMPLICATED HISTORY WITH THE CONFEDERATE FLAG |last=Irwin |first=Corey |date=June 14, 2020 |publisher=Ultimate Classic Rock |access-date=September 20, 2021}}</ref>\n}}\n| years_active     = 1987\u2013present<!--All Music Guide says 1987-->\n| label            = {{flatlist|\n* [[Atlantic Records|Atlantic]]\n* [[Audium Entertainment|Audium]]\n* [[Shanachie Records|Shanachie]]\n* [[Koch Entertainment|E1 Music]]\n* D&B Masterworks\n}}\n| website          = {{URL|confederaterailroad.net}}\n| current_members  = * [[Danny Shirley]]\n* Rusty Hendrix\n* Mark DuFresne\n* Mo Thaxton\n| past_members     = * Jimmy Dormire\n* Chris McDaniel\n* Michael Lamb\n* Warren \"Gates\" Nichols\n* Cody McCarver\n* Bobby Randall\n* Wayne Secrest\n* Joey Recker\n}}\n'''Confederate Railroad''' (originally known as \"Confederate RR\") is an American [[country rock]] band founded in 1987 in [[Marietta, Georgia]], by [[Danny Shirley]] (lead vocals), Michael Lamb (lead guitar), Mark Dufresne (drums), Chris McDaniel (keyboards), Warren \"Gates\" Nichols (steel guitar), and Wayne Secrest (bass guitar). After serving as a backing band for [[outlaw country]] acts [[David Allan Coe]] and [[Johnny Paycheck]], the band signed to a recording contract with [[Atlantic Records]], releasing their self-titled debut album that year. In the 1990s, they released four more albums for Atlantic.\n\nConfederate Railroad has released six studio albums. In addition, 18 of their singles have entered the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts.\n\nThe band's most recent studio album, ''Lucky to Be Alive'', was issued on the D&B Masterworks label on July 15, 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.timesfreepress.com/news/life/entertainment/story/2016/jul/15/not-ready-retire-work-just-keeps-coming-confe/375866/|title=Hixson's Danny Shirley and the Confederate Railroad still in demand 40 years after his professional debut|date=15 July 2016 |access-date=2016-08-05}}</ref> The band released their first live album, ''Confederate Railroad Live: Back to the Barrooms'', on the [[Koch Entertainment|E1 Music]] label on June 15, 2010.\n\n==History==\nConfederate Railroad was founded in 1987 by [[Danny Shirley]], Michael Lamb, Gates Nichols (May 26, 1944 \u2013 August 14, 2009),<ref name=obit1/> Chris McDaniel, Wayne Secrest (April 29, 1950 \u2013 June 2, 2018),<ref name=obit2/> and Mark Dufresne. The six members began playing at bars in and around [[Atlanta, Georgia]], and Augusta, Georgia.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p33597}}</ref> Over time, they also worked as a road band for [[David Allan Coe]] and [[Johnny Paycheck]]. Shirley had previously been signed to the Amor [[record label]] as a solo singer, charting five times on the country charts between 1984 and 1988.<ref name=\"whitburnshirley\">{{cite book|title=Hot Country Songs 1944 to 2008|last=Whitburn|first=Joel|publisher=Record Research, Inc.|year=2008|isbn=978-0-89820-177-2|page=380}}<!--|access-date=2009-10-06--></ref>\n\nAfter several years in the Atlanta area, the band signed with [[Atlantic Records]] in 1992 and released its [[Confederate Railroad (album)|self-titled]] debut album. The album produced six hit singles and was certified 2\u00d7 Platinum in the U.S.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> In 1993, Confederate Railroad was awarded Best New Group at the [[Academy of Country Music|ACM]] awards.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://countrymusic.about.com/library/reviews/aaprunleashed.htm|title=Who Is Country Star David Allan Coe?|access-date=2007-03-02|archive-date=2011-09-28|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110928045419/http://countrymusic.about.com/library/reviews/aaprunleashed.htm|url-status=dead}}</ref> In order of release, these singles were \"She Took It Like a Man,\" \"Jesus and Mama,\" \"[[Queen of Memphis]],\" (their highest chart peak, at no.&nbsp;2) \"When You Leave That Way You Can Never Go Back,\" \"[[Trashy Women]],\" and \"She Never Cried.\"\n\n''[[Notorious (Confederate Railroad album)|Notorious]]'' was the band's second album. Released in 1994, it was certified platinum as well. The album was led off by the no.&nbsp;9 \"[[Daddy Never Was the Cadillac Kind]],\" followed by the no.&nbsp;20 \"Elvis and Andy,\" and finally \"Summer in Dixie,\" which failed to make Top 40. Also in 1994, Shirley and [[Mark Collie]] co-wrote and sang guest vocals on [[Billy Ray Cyrus]]'s \"Redneck Heaven,\" an album cut from his 1994 disc ''[[Storm in the Heartland]]''.<ref>{{Cite AV media notes |title=Storm in the Heartland |others=Billy Ray Cyrus |year=1994 |type=CD booklet |publisher=Mercury Records |id=314-526 081-2}}</ref>\n\nOne year later, the band released its third album, 1995's ''[[When and Where]]''. This album failed to sell as well as its predecessors, and was less successful on the charts as well. Lead-off single \"When and Where\" reached No.&nbsp;24, while the other three singles \u2013 \"Bill's Laundromat, Bar and Grill,\" \"When He Was My Age,\" and \"See Ya\" all failed to reach Top 40. A ''[[Greatest Hits (Confederate Railroad album)|Greatest Hits]]'' package followed in 1996.\n\nIn 1998, the band released its fourth and final studio album for Atlantic, titled ''Keep on Rockin'''. Its only two singles were \"The Big One\" and \"Cowboy Cadillac,\" both of which failed to reach the Top 60 on the country singles charts. After another compilation titled ''Rockin' Country Party Pack'' (which produced another chart single in \"Toss a Little Bone,\" previously from ''When and Where''), the band exited Atlantic.\n\nOne year later, Confederate Railroad signed to Audium/Koch Records (now [[E1 Music]]) for its fifth studio album, ''Unleashed''. It was led off by the no.&nbsp;39 \"What Brothers Do.\" Although this was the band's first Top 40 country hit since \"When and Where\" in 1995, the other singles \u2013 \"She Treats Her Body Like a Temple\" and \"White Trash with Money\" \u2013 both failed to reach Top 40.\n\nThe band did not record again until 2007's ''Cheap Thrills'', an album of [[cover song]]s. This album was led off by a cover of \"[[Please Come to Boston]],\" which failed to chart.\n\nConfederate Railroad members signed a record deal with E1 Music in 2010 and released their first-ever live album called \"Confederate Railroad Live: Back to the Barrooms.\" Cody McCarver of Confederate Railroad also signed to the label and has recently had success{{vague|date=April 2020}} with Confederate Railroad's song \"White Trash with Money\" which was written by Confederate Railroad's Danny Shirley with songwriter Buck Moore. The video by Cody also featured Jimmy Dormire who left Confederate Railroad in 2008. Cody McCarver released a single and video called \"I'm America.\"\n\nSince 2019, the band has missed bookings and had concerts cancelled because of concerns over the band's name and their logo's inclusion of two [[Confederate flag]]s. In cancelling their planned performance at the [[Ulster County, New York#Recreation|Ulster County Fair]], organizers said the event must represent \"the values of all members of our community\" and that \"showcasing of a symbol of division and racism runs counter to that principle.\"\n\nCritics say that the Confederate flag is a racist symbol, representing a [[United States Civil War|war to continue slavery]] and [[racial segregation in the United States]].<ref>{{cite web|last=Kaur |first=Harmeet |url=https://www.cnn.com/2019/08/01/entertainment/confederate-railroad-name-backlash-trnd/index.html |title=Confederate Railroad says it won't change its name |publisher=CNN |date=2019-08-01 |access-date=2020-04-04}}</ref> The band said the cancellation was \"very disappointing\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.confederaterailroad.com/press-release.htm |title=Press release |publisher=Confederate Railroad |access-date=2020-04-04}}</ref> Shirley says the flag represents history and Southern heritage.<ref>{{cite web|agency=Associated Press |url=https://www.sj-r.com/news/20190725/country-band-confederate-railroad-nixed-from-another-fair |title=Country band Confederate Railroad nixed from another fair - News - The State Journal-Register - Springfield, IL |publisher=Sj-r.com |date=2019-07-25 |access-date=2020-04-04}}</ref>\n\nShirley blamed [[J. B. Pritzker|Governor J. B. Pritzker]]'s cancellation of the band from the [[DuQuoin State Fair]] lineup on [[political correctness]], which he says is focused on the band's name. The governor's office said that state resources could not be used \"to promote symbols of racism,\" specifying the Confederate flag in the group's logo.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Hudak |first=Joseph |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/confederate-railroad-band-name-canceled-shows-875639/ |title=Confederate Railroad Singer Talks Band Name Controversy |magazine=Rolling Stone |date=2019-08-23 |access-date=2020-04-04}}</ref>\n\nShirley suffered a broken back on April 1, 2021.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/danny-shirley-confederate-railroad-lead-singer-broken-back/|title = Danny Shirley, Confederate Railroad Lead Singer, Suffers Broken Back| date=April 2021 }}</ref>\n\nIn 2022, the band toured the US as a 4-piece band with Shirley on lead vocals and guitar, Rusty Hendrix on lead guitar, Mo Thaxton on bass and occasional lead vocals, and Mark DuFresne on drums.\n\n==Musical stylings==\nDescribed vocally as a \"gruff, reliable twanger,\"<ref name=\"new2\">{{cite journal |last=Dickinson |first=Chris |date=August 1995 |title=Confederate Railroad - ''When and Where'' review |journal=New Country |volume=2 |issue=10 |page=62}}</ref> lead singer Danny Shirley cites [[outlaw country]] acts such as [[Waylon Jennings]] as his major influence.<ref name=\"new\">{{cite journal |last=Mansfield |first=Brian |date=April 1994 |title=When Good Things Happen to Rough People: Confederate Railroad Stays on the Country Side of the Tracks |journal=New Country |volume=1 |issue=3 |pages=36\u201339}}</ref> According to him, the band's music is \"straight-ahead outlaw country,\"<ref name=\"new\"/> although their image has also drawn comparisons to [[Southern rock]].<ref name=\"allmusic\"/>\n\nConfederate Railroad's novelty numbers, such as \"Trashy Women,\" show a tongue-in-cheek sense of humor. A reviewer for ''New Country'' magazine wrote that they are \"one of the few bands who can pull off a song about how they prefer trashy women and sound like they really mean it.\"<ref name=\"new2\"/><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.tntbooking.com/bios/confederate_railroad.htm|title=T&T Management and Booking Agency - Confederate Railroad|website=www.tntbooking.com|access-date=2007-03-02|archive-date=2006-11-09|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061109111752/http://www.tntbooking.com/bios/confederate_railroad.htm|url-status=dead}}</ref> A more serious side of the band is shown in their ballads. Those on ''Notorious'', for instance, were described by ''New Country'' magazine as \"show[ing] men left stunned and confused by a world that changed faster than they could follow.\"<ref name=\"new\"/>\n\n==Member changes==\nLead guitarist Michael Lamb, one of the group's original members, left in the mid 1990s and was replaced with Jimmy Dormire.\n\nChris McDaniel, the original keyboardist, left and was replaced with Cody McCarver.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> McCarver has released a solo album, although he continued to tour as a member of Confederate Railroad up until his last performance with them at the Putnam County Fair in [[Eleanor, West Virginia]], on July 16, 2010. To Date, Cody has released 2 Country Music Albums & 4 Gospel Albums. He's also worked on some Western Independent Films and his most recent work was with [[John Schneider (screen actor)|John Schneider]] working on his album and being a costar in his movie \"Stand on It\" as well as the sequel \"Poker Run.\" He is currently on the road touring with John Schneider in his band where he also opens the show with his own music.\n\nIn June 2008, Jimmy Dormire announced that he was leaving Confederate Railroad to continue his solo career, though he continues as a member of Cody McCarver's band. Dormire was subsequently replaced by Rusty Hendrix, former side man for Mark Wills and Sammy Kershaw. Jimmy was part of the Cody McCarver band, and became a regular in the John Schneider band before joining to Country Band [[BlackHawk (band)|BlackHawk]] and the [[Outlaws (band)|Outlaws]] as a Full time Member.\n\nGates Nichols retired from Confederate Railroad in December 2008, and in July of the following year, he was diagnosed with pancreatic cancer. He died from the disease on the morning of August 14, 2009, at the age of 65.<ref name=obit1>{{cite news|url=https://www.samclarkfuneralhome.com/obituary/Warren-Nichols|title=Welcome to the memorial page for Warren Nichols May 26, 1944 ~ August 14, 2009 (age 65)|website=samclarkfuneralhome.com |access-date=May 6, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.confederaterailroad.net/news.htm|title=Confederate Railroad - News|website=www.confederaterailroad.net}}</ref> Nearly two years later, in January 2011, Bobby Randall joined Confederate Railroad, playing steel guitar and fiddle for 6 years until his departure in 2017.\n\nIn October 2014, Mo Thaxton joined the group on the baritone,{{vague|date=August 2019}} bass and vocals. Thaxton was a member of the group [[Dr. Hook & the Medicine Show|Dr. Hook]] for 12 years prior to joining Confederate Railroad.\n\nJoey Recker began playing piano with the group in January 2017 after 28 years in the Armed Forces. He continued on with Confederate Railroad until he decided to depart the band December 2021 to be closer to his family and focus on his faith. He fronts the Joey & Shug Duo that does local music and a Southern Gospel band called Antioch-Southern Gospel.\n\nBassist Wayne Secrest retired from the band in October 2017. He died on June 2, 2018, after a long illness, at the age of 68.<ref name=obit2>{{cite news|url=https://www.pricebrothersfh.com/obituary/Wayne-Secrest|title=Wayne Allen Secrest April 29, 1950 ~ June 2, 2018 (age 68)|website=pricebrothersfh.com |access-date=May 7, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.allaccess.com/net-news/archive/story/177213/confederate-railroad-founding-member-wayne-secrest|title=Confederate Railroad Founding Member Wayne Secrest Dies At Age 68}}</ref>\n\n==Solo work==\nIn addition to his work in the band, frontman [[Danny Shirley]] made a guest appearance alongside [[Mark Collie]] on the song \"Redneck Heaven\" from [[Billy Ray Cyrus]]' 1994 album ''[[Storm in the Heartland]]'', a song which Collie and Shirley co-wrote. Danny Shirley has released 3 albums prior to starting the Confederate Railroad Band. His first, \"Local Legend,\" was released in 1984 on Amor Records. His second, \"Far From Over,\" and third \"I Make the Living\" albums were released in 1990 also on Amor. Danny released a 2 CD album featuring several of the songs from those 3 albums called \"The Pyramid Collection\" in 2005.\n\nCody McCarver released a self-titled solo album for the Aspirion label in 2006, which produced the singles \"Red Flag\" and \"Through God's Eyes.\" He released another single, \"Look What You've Done,\" in 2009. His 2010 single \"White Trash With Money\" was written by fellow band member Shirley along with songwriter Buck Moore. \"White Trash With Money\" was followed by \"I'm America.\" Since recording two country albums, Cody went on to release four gospel albums and is currently acting in films along with [[John Schneider (screen actor)|John Schneider]] and playing in Schneider's band.\n\nIn 2022, Bassist Mo Thaxton recorded a Bluegrass album \"The Mo Show\" that was released in 2023. He recorded 2 Railroad songs \"Don't feel as young as I used to\" & \"Between the rainbows and the rain\". This CD is only available at their shows and sold exclusively by Mo himself.\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:14em;\"| Title\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Kevin_Costner_&_Modern_West","to":"Kevin Costner & Modern West"}],"pages":{"26339434":{"pageid":26339434,"ns":0,"title":"Kevin Costner & Modern West","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country rock band}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Kevin Costner & Modern West\n| image               = Costner and Modern West, 2010.jpg\n| caption             =\n| image_size          = 250\n| landscape           = yes\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              =\n| genre               = [[Country rock]], [[country music|country]]\n| years_active        = 2007\u2013present\n| label               = [[Show Dog-Universal Music|Universal South]]\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             = [(hacked) redirects somewhere else Official Website]\n| current_members     = [[Kevin Costner]]<br/> John Coinman<br/> Teddy Morgan<br/> Blair Forward<br/> Larry Cobb<br/> Park Chisolm<br/> Luke Bulla<br/> Bobby Yang<br/> Roddy Chong\n| past_members        =\n}}\n\n'''Kevin Costner & Modern West''' is an American [[country rock]] band founded and fronted by actor [[Kevin Costner]]. He began a worldwide tour with the band in October 2007, which included shows in Istanbul and Rome. It also performed at NASCAR Sprint Cup Series races at Daytona International Speedway and Lowe's Motor Speedway in [[Concord, North Carolina]].\n\nThe band released its first country album, ''[[Untold Truths]]'', on November 11, 2008, on Universal South Records. It peaked at No.&nbsp;61 on the ''Billboard'' Top Country Albums chart and No.&nbsp;35 on the Top Heatseekers chart. Three singles (\"Superman 14\", \"Long Hot Night\" and \"Backyard\") have been released to radio, although none have charted. Videos were made for the songs \"Superman 14\", \"Backyard\" and \"Hey Man What About You\".\n\nIn 2009, Costner went on tour with the band and special guests The Alternate Routes. In August, at the Big Valley Jamboree in Camrose, Alberta, Costner and the band were scheduled next on stage when a severe thunderstorm struck, causing the stage and stands on the main stage to collapse. One person was reported dead and forty wounded.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2009/08/02/world/AP-CN-Canada-Stage-Collapse.html?_r=1 |title=1 Dead, 40 Injured in Canada Stage Collapse |newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|date=August 2, 2009 |accessdate=August 2, 2009}}{{dead link|date=February 2014}}</ref> Later, an auction was held to raise money for the two young sons of the woman killed. A dinner with Costner was auctioned for $41,000. Two guitars, one autographed by Costner, helped raise another $10,000 each.<ref>{{cite news |first=Nick |last=Lees |title=Katz likely culprit behind mystery $41,000 bid |url=https://www.pressreader.com/canada/edmonton-journal/20090812/281882999355295 |work=Edmonton Journal |date=August 12, 2009 |page=B3}}</ref>\n\nIn February 2010, Kevin Costner & Modern West released their second album, ''Turn It On'', only in Europe. To support the album the band toured Europe, with ''Turn It On'' reaching the album charts in Germany, Austria, Switzerland and Greece. The first single from the album, \"Let Me Be the One\", with special guest Sara Beck singing with Costner, was also made as a music video. A third album, ''From Where I Stand'', was released in 2011 and included vocals from the German pop singer [[Nena]]. In April 2012, the band played a benefit gala for the [[Adrienne Arsht Center for the Performing Arts]] in Miami, Florida.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n!
